كما أنَّهما يخالفان سمعنا وبصرنا أيضاً في الذات، فهما صفتان قدیمتان قائمتان بذاته تعالى، وأمَّا سمعنا وبصرنا فحادثان قائمان بمحل مخصوص : - فبصرنا قائم بإنسان العين أو هو : قوَّة مودعة في العصبتين المجوفتين اللتين يتلاقيان ثم يفترقان، كما هو مذهب الحكماء. - وسمعنا قائم بالصِّماخ ؛ أي: ثقب الأذن، أو هو : قوَّةٌ قائمة بالعصب المفروش في مقعر الصماخ. والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، وسمعنا وبصرنا من أسباب علومنا بخلاف سمعه وبصره تعالى . الأجسام والألوان معاً لا الألوان فقط هو مذهب أهل السُّنَّة، خلافاً للمعتزلة القائلين : المرئي الألوان فقط . قوله : (بإنسان (العين) أي : النُّقطة الصغيرة التي في وسط السواد. قوله : ( مودعة ) : أي : كائنة ومستقرة . قوله : (اللَّتين يتلاقيان) أي: ويتقاطعان تقاطعاً صليبياً، وقيل: يتلاقيان ثم يرجعان ؛ كالدالين المقلوبتين ظهر إحديهما في ظهر الأخرى، فقول الشارح: (ثم يفترقان) مرور على القول الثاني، وهذان القولان للفلاسفة . قوله : (من أسباب علومنا أي فإذا رأينا أو سمعنا شيئاً؛ نعلم بسبب ذلك معاني تقوم بعقولنا
As they also differ from our hearing and sight in essence, for they are two eternal attributes subsisting by His essence, while our hearing and sight are contingent, subsisting in a specific locus: our sight subsists in the pupil of the eye, or it is a power deposited in the two hollow optic nerves that meet and then separate, according to the philosophers; and our hearing subsists in the ear canal, i.e., the hole of the ear, or it is a power subsisting in the nerve spread in the concavity of the ear canal. Allah is exalted above that, and our hearing and sight are causes of our knowledge, unlike His hearing and sight. That bodies and colors together, not colors alone, are seen is the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna, contrary to the Mu'tazila who say: only colors are seen. His saying: 'bi-insān al-'ayn' i.e., the small spot in the middle of the black part. His saying: 'mūda'a' i.e., existing and settled. His saying: 'allatayni yaltaqiyāni' i.e., and they cross crosswise, and it is said they meet and then return, like two reversed dals with the back of one against the back of the other; the commentator's saying 'then they separate' is based on the second opinion, and these two opinions are of the philosophers. His saying: 'min asbāb 'ulūminā' i.e., when we see or hear something, we know due to that meanings that come to our minds.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a theological explanation of the divine attributes of hearing and sight. It begins by affirming that Allah's hearing and sight are eternal attributes subsisting in His essence, unlike human hearing and sight which are contingent and dependent on physical organs. The author then details the physical basis of human sight (the pupil and optic nerves) and hearing (the ear canal and auditory nerve) according to the philosophers, emphasizing that Allah is free from such physicality. A key distinction is that human senses are causes of knowledge, whereas divine senses are not. The passage then addresses a theological dispute: Ahl al-Sunna hold that what is seen (by Allah or in the afterlife) includes both bodies and colors, whereas the Mu'tazila restrict visibility to colors alone. The remainder of the passage provides lexical and anatomical glosses on the earlier text, clarifying terms such as 'insān al-'ayn' (pupil), 'mūda'a' (deposited), and the description of the optic nerves.

The Sunni Position on What Is Seen: Bodies and Colors
States the Sunni view on what is seen, contrasting with Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that both bodies and colors are visible to Allah and in the afterlife, and how this differs from the Mu'tazilite view.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunna say bodies and colors are seen; the Mu'tazila say only colors.

After establishing the nature of divine senses, the author turns to a related theological debate: what can be seen? Specifically, what is visible to Allah and what will be seen in the afterlife? The Sunni school maintains that both bodies and colors are visible, while the Mu'tazila restrict visibility to colors alone. This brief but sharp statement encapsulates a major disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic sentence and its translation. Note that it is a single declarative statement.
2
Identify the two opposing views
Find the Sunni position (bodies and colors) and the Mu'tazilite position (colors only).
The author clearly labels each side.
3
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this issue matters. It is connected to the vision of Allah (ru'ya) in the afterlife.
The Mu'tazila argued that only colors are seen, so Allah—neither body nor color—cannot be seen. The Sunnis argued the opposite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما أنَّهما يخالفان سمعنا وبصرنا أيضاً في الذات، فهما صفتان قدیمتان قائمتان بذاته تعالى، وأمَّا سمعنا وبصرنا فحادثان قائمان بمحل مخصوص : - فبصرنا قائم بإنسان العين أو هو : قوَّة مودعة في العصبتين المجوفتين اللتين يتلاقيان ثم يفترقان، كما هو مذهب الحكماء. - وسمعنا قائم بالصِّماخ ؛ أي: ثقب الأذن، أو هو : قوَّةٌ قائمة بالعصب المفروش في مقعر الصماخ. والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، وسمعنا وبصرنا من أسباب علومنا بخلاف سمعه وبصره تعالى . الأجسام والألوان معاً لا الألوان فقط هو مذهب أهل السُّنَّة، خلافاً للمعتزلة القائلين : المرئي الألوان فقط . قوله : (بإنسان (العين) أي : النُّقطة الصغيرة التي في وسط السواد. قوله : ( مودعة ) : أي : كائنة ومستقرة . قوله : (اللَّتين يتلاقيان) أي: ويتقاطعان تقاطعاً صليبياً، وقيل: يتلاقيان ثم يرجعان ؛ كالدالين المقلوبتين ظهر إحديهما في ظهر الأخرى، فقول الشارح: (ثم يفترقان) مرور على القول الثاني، وهذان القولان للفلاسفة . قوله : (من أسباب علومنا أي فإذا رأينا أو سمعنا شيئاً؛ نعلم بسبب ذلك معاني تقوم بعقولنا
As they also differ from our hearing and sight in essence, for they are two eternal attributes subsisting by His essence, while our hearing and sight are contingent, subsisting in a specific locus: our sight subsists in the pupil of the eye, or it is a power deposited in the two hollow optic nerves that meet and then separate, according to the philosophers; and our hearing subsists in the ear canal, i.e., the hole of the ear, or it is a power subsisting in the nerve spread in the concavity of the ear canal. Allah is exalted above that, and our hearing and sight are causes of our knowledge, unlike His hearing and sight. That bodies and colors together, not colors alone, are seen is the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna, contrary to the Mu'tazila who say: only colors are seen. His saying: 'bi-insān al-'ayn' i.e., the small spot in the middle of the black part. His saying: 'mūda'a' i.e., existing and settled. His saying: 'allatayni yaltaqiyāni' i.e., and they cross crosswise, and it is said they meet and then return, like two reversed dals with the back of one against the back of the other; the commentator's saying 'then they separate' is based on the second opinion, and these two opinions are of the philosophers. His saying: 'min asbāb 'ulūminā' i.e., when we see or hear something, we know due to that meanings that come to our minds.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a theological explanation of the divine attributes of hearing and sight. It begins by affirming that Allah's hearing and sight are eternal attributes subsisting in His essence, unlike human hearing and sight which are contingent and dependent on physical organs. The author then details the physical basis of human sight (the pupil and optic nerves) and hearing (the ear canal and auditory nerve) according to the philosophers, emphasizing that Allah is free from such physicality. A key distinction is that human senses are causes of knowledge, whereas divine senses are not. The passage then addresses a theological dispute: Ahl al-Sunna hold that what is seen (by Allah or in the afterlife) includes both bodies and colors, whereas the Mu'tazila restrict visibility to colors alone. The remainder of the passage provides lexical and anatomical glosses on the earlier text, clarifying terms such as 'insān al-'ayn' (pupil), 'mūda'a' (deposited), and the description of the optic nerves.

المعتزلة
مرئي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: The Mu'tazila believe that both bodies and colors are seen.
Correction: The passage states that the Mu'tazila say only colors are seen, while Ahl al-Sunna say both bodies and colors.

The Three Relations of Hearing and Sight
Lists the three kinds of relations of hearing and sight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three kinds of relations (actual eternal, potential eternal, actual temporal) that the attributes of hearing and sight have.

Core Idea
Allah's hearing and sight relate to creation in three distinct modes, eternal and temporal.

The divine attributes of hearing and sight are not simple; they have multiple relations. In this passage, the author explains three types of relations: an eternal actual relation, an eternal potential relation, and a temporal actual relation. Understanding these helps avoid confusion about how Allah's attributes relate to created things.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then the literal translation. Notice the three terms: تنجيزي قديم, صلوحي قديم, تنجيزي حادث.
These terms are technical and will be explained.
2
Identify the three relations
The passage names three relations. Write them down: 1) eternal actual, 2) eternal potential, 3) temporal actual.
Each relation has a different scope.
3
Understand 'actual' vs 'potential'
Actual means the relation is fully realized; potential means it is not yet realized but possible. Eternal means it exists from eternity; temporal means it begins in time.
This distinction is crucial.
4
Reflect on the clarification in commentary
The hashiya explains that 'eternal potential with our essences' means before our existence. So Allah's hearing and sight are potentially related to us before we are created.
This prevents misunderstanding that the relation only begins when we exist.
5
Test your understanding with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to see if you can identify the meaning of 'eternal potential'.
Review the passage if needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهما تعلُّقات ثلاثة : تنجيزي قديم بتعلقات السمع والبصر وصفاته تعالى، وصلوحي قديم بذواتنا وصفاتنا، وتنجيزي حادث عند وجودنا. قوله : (وصلوحي قديم بذواتنا وصفاتنا) : أي : قبل وجودنا
They have three relations: an eternal actual relation to the objects of hearing and sight and to His attributes; an eternal potential relation to our essences and attributes; and a temporal actual relation upon our existence. His saying: 'and eternal potential with our essences and attributes' means: before our existence.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage enumerates the three kinds of relations (ta'alluqāt) that belong to the divine attributes of hearing and sight. The first is an 'eternal actual' relation (tanzīzī qadīm): this is the relation that holds eternally with respect to the objects of hearing and sight themselves (i.e., what is heard and seen) as well as with Allah's own attributes. The second is an 'eternal potential' relation (ṣulūḥī qadīm): this is the relation that holds eternally in the sense of potentiality regarding our essences and attributes, meaning that before we exist, Allah's hearing and sight are potentially related to us. The third is a 'temporal actual' relation (tanzīzī ḥādith): this occurs when we come into existence, at which point the relation becomes actual. The hashiya clarifies that 'eternal potential with our essences and attributes' means 'before our existence,' i.e., it is a potential relation that becomes actual when we exist.

Key Terms
تعلق
تنجيزي
صلوحي
قديم
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the relation of Allah's attributes to creation is only actual when creation exists.
Correction: There is an eternal potential relation that exists before creation, and an eternal actual relation to His own attributes and the objects of hearing/sight.

Checkpoint
What does 'eternal potential' (صلوحي قديم) mean in the context of the relations of hearing and sight?
A) A relation that is actual from eternity to creation
B) A relation that exists potentially before creation
C) A relation that begins at the time of creation
D) A relation that exists only in the divine essence

Key Takeaway
The three relations of hearing and sight are eternal actual, eternal potential, and temporal actual, each with a distinct scope.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Allah's hearing was potentially related to you before you existed. Now that you exist, it is actually related. Does this awareness change how you speak when you think no one is listening? What will you do today to honor that His hearing is always actual for you?
?
The eternal actual relation of Allah's hearing to His own attributes means His self-awareness is perfect. When you speak, you are heard by One whose own speech is flawless. How does that confront the carelessness of your words? Will you commit to one hour today of mindful speech?
?
Before you were born, Allah's sight was potentially related to you. Now it is actually related. Your actions are seen. Does that make you feel watched or cared for? What action will you change because you know He sees it?

The Intrinsic Eternity of the Attributes of Meanings
Al-Sawi defends intrinsic eternity of attributes and refutes the cause view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the attributes of meanings (sifāt al-ma‘ānī) are eternal by their own essences, not merely through the divine essence, and why the alternative view is considered disrespectful and unfounded.

Core Idea
The attributes of meanings are intrinsically eternal, not caused by Allah's essence.

In this passage, Imam al-Sawi defends the orthodox Ash'ari position on the eternity of the divine attributes of knowledge, power, and will. He firmly rejects a view held by some scholars that these attributes are eternal only because Allah's essence is their cause. His sharp critique underscores the high level of theological adab (propriety) required when speaking about Allah. Let's examine the passage closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the strong language used to reject the alternative view.
2
Identify the correct doctrine
Find the statement that the attributes of meanings are eternal by their own essences (قديمة بذاتها). Note the emphasis on intrinsic eternity (ذاتي).
The author says their eternity is intrinsic and they are not possible in themselves.
3
Understand the rejected view
Locate the phrase 'or that His essence is a cause in them'. This is the view being criticized. The author clarifies that 'or' here means 'and'.
The view implies the attributes are not eternal by themselves but depend on Allah's essence as a cause.
4
Note the refutation
Read why the author calls this view 'repugnant' (شنيع) and accuses it of disrespect. See that he says there is no proof for it.
5
Recognize the scholars involved
Identify that Fakhr al-Razi, al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani), and al-Baydawi are named as holding the view, and that Ibn al-Tilimsani rebuked al-Razi.
This shows the internal criticism within Sunni scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أن صفات المعاني قديمة بذاتها. وكلها أي صفات المعاني قديمة بالذات أي بذاتها؛ أي إن قدمها ذاتي وليست بممكنة في نفسها، وإنما قدمها بقدم الذات المقدس، أو أن ذاته تعالى علة فيها، كما قال بذلك بعض علماء أهل السنة وهو قول شنيع، تمجه قلوب الصالحين العارفين بربهم، إذ لا يخفى ما فيه من إساءة الأدب بمقام الله الأعز الأحمى، مع أنه لا حجة على ارتكابه، بل الحجة قائمة على ما ذكرنا، كما أشرت له بقولي: قوله: (أو أن ذاته تعالى علة فيها) : (أو) بمعنى الواو؛ لأن هذا هو معنى قوله: وإنما قدمها بقدم الذات. قوله: (بعض علماء أهل السنة) أي: وهو الفخر الرازي، وتبعه السعد والبيضاوي وجماعة، وشنع ابن التلمساني على الفخر بقوله: (1) ينظر شرح العقائد النسفية (ص 81).
An exposition that the attributes of meanings are eternal by their own essences. And all of them—i.e., the attributes of meanings—are eternal by essence, i.e., by their own essence; meaning that their eternity is intrinsic and they are not possible in themselves, but rather their eternity is through the eternity of the sacred essence, or that His essence is a cause in them, as some scholars of Ahl al-Sunna have said. And it is a repugnant saying, which the hearts of the righteous knowers of their Lord reject, for it is not hidden what it contains of disrespect to the station of Allah the Most Mighty and Most Protected. Moreover, there is no proof for adopting it, rather the proof is established for what we have mentioned, as I have indicated with my saying: His saying: 'or that His essence is a cause in them'—'or' here is in the sense of 'and', because this is the meaning of his saying: 'rather its eternity is through the eternity of the essence.' His saying: 'some scholars of Ahl al-Sunna' i.e., Fakhr al-Razi, followed by al-Sa'd and al-Baydawi and a group, and Ibn al-Tilimsani rebuked al-Razi with his saying: (1) see Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya p. 81.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument and refutation. It begins by stating the correct doctrine: the attributes of meanings (sifāt al-ma‘ānī)—such as knowledge, power, and will—are eternal by their own essences. The author emphasizes that their eternity is intrinsic (dhātī), meaning they are not merely possible beings that have been granted eternity by the divine essence. He then rejects an alternative view held by some scholars of Ahl al-Sunna, namely that the divine essence is a cause (‘illa) for their eternity. He calls this view 'repugnant' (shanī‘) and accuses it of disrespect (sū’ al-adab) towards Allah. He insists there is no proof for this view, and that the proof supports his own position. The hashiya clarifies that the word 'or' in the phrase 'or that His essence is a cause' actually means 'and' (wāw), linking it to the previous statement. Finally, he identifies the proponents of the rejected view: Fakhr al-Razi, followed by al-Sa‘d (i.e., al-Taftazani) and al-Baydawi, and notes that Ibn al-Tilimsani rebuked al-Razi for it.

Key Terms

قديمة بالذات
ذاتي
ممكنة
علة
فخر الرازي
السعد
البيضاوي
ابن التلمساني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The attributes of meanings are eternal because Allah's essence is their cause.
Correction: They are intrinsically eternal by themselves; viewing the divine essence as a cause is disrespectful and lacks proof.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the correct view regarding the eternity of the attributes of meanings?
A) They are eternal because Allah's essence is a cause for them
B) They are eternal by their own essences
C) They are possible and become eternal through Allah
D) They are not eternal

Key Takeaway
The attributes of meanings are eternal by their own essences, and viewing the divine essence as a cause for their eternity is disrespectful and unsupported by proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself thinking of Allah's attributes as merely 'tools' He uses, rather than eternal realities that are inseparable from His essence? How might that diminish your reverence for Him in your prayer and daily life?
?
The author calls the view that attributes are caused by Allah's essence 'repugnant' and an insult to divine dignity. Is there any belief you hold about Allah that, if examined, might be out of tune with His majesty? What will you do to correct it starting today?
?
If you truly internalized that Allah's knowledge is eternal by its very nature, not something He 'acquired' or 'created', would you trust His knowledge of your hidden sins and struggles more deeply? How would that change your repentance?

The Three Attachments of the Attributes of Hearing and Sight
Enumeration of the three attachments of divine attributes of hearing and sight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of attachments belonging to Allah's attributes of hearing and sight and how they relate to eternity and temporality.

Core Idea
The attributes of hearing and sight have both eternal and temporal attachments.

In this lesson, we examine a concise enumeration from Sanusi's text on the attributes of hearing and sight. The author distinguishes three attachments: two are eternal in different respects, and one is temporal. This classification helps clarify how God's attributes relate to creation both before and after existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully and then the literal translation. Notice the three terms.
The terms 'tanzīzī' and 'sulūḥī' are technical.
2
Identify the three attachments
List the three attachments and note the differences: two are 'qadīm' (eternal) and one is 'ḥādith' (temporal).
The first and third are 'tanzīzī' (actualizing), the second is 'sulūḥī' (potential).
3
Understand the commentary
Read the teacher commentary to see how the second attachment is potential and eternal before our existence.
The commentator clarifies that 'sulūḥī' means potential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهما تعلقات ثلاثة: تنجيزي قديم بذاته تعالى، وصلوحي قديم بذواتنا وصفاتنا، وتنجيزي حادث عند وجودنا. قوله: (وصلوحي قديم بذاتنا وصفاتنا): أي: قبل وجودنا.
And they have three attachments: an actualizing eternal by His essence exalted, a potential eternal by our essences and attributes, and an actualizing temporal at our existence. His saying: (and a potential eternal by our essences and attributes): i.e., before our existence.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage enumerates the three attachments (ta‘alluqāt) of the attributes of hearing and sight. The first is an actualizing attachment (tanzīzī) that is eternal by God's essence itself. The second is a potential attachment (sulūḥī) that is eternal by our essences and attributes, meaning it exists in potentiality before we actually exist. The third is an actualizing attachment that comes into existence when we exist. The commentator clarifies that the phrase 'potential eternal by our essences and attributes' means this attachment is present before our existence. This classification shows how these attributes relate to objects of perception both eternally and temporally.

Key Takeaway

?
The potential eternal attachment is by our essences and attributes—before we existed. What does that tell you about your significance in God's eternal plan? How does that humble you and yet give you purpose? What will you do today to live up to that eternal relation?

The Eternity of the Attributes of Meanings
Definition and refutation of causal view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the attributes of meanings are eternal by essence, not by being caused, and why the view that God's essence is a cause for them is a grave error.

Core Idea
Attributes of meanings are eternal intrinsically, not through a cause.

Sanusi begins by affirming the eternity of the attributes of meanings, explaining that their eternity is intrinsic. He then warns against the false belief that God's essence is a cause for the attributes, a view attributed to al-Fakhr al-Razi and condemned as a serious breach of adab.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the positive statement
Read the opening lines carefully: the attributes of meanings are eternal by their own essences. Note that the commentator explains this means their eternity is intrinsic.
The word 'qadīm' here means eternal, not old.
2
Identify the deviant view
Find the phrase 'او ان ذاته تعالى علة فيها'. This is the causal view that God's essence is a cause of the attributes.
The commentator strongly condemns this as a heinous statement.
3
Understand the refutation
Read the commentator's critique: this view lacks evidence and contradicts proper adab toward God. Then see the argument: the attributes are not other than the essence and inseparable, so they cannot be 'possible' requiring a cause.
Ibn al-Tilimsani's refutation is key here.
4
See the slippery consequence
Note that al-Razi's statement parallels the philosophers' claim about the world, which is rejected as a false creed that undermines Ahl al-Sunna.
This shows how a small error can lead to major doctrinal harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أن صفات المعاني قديمة بذاتها. وكلها أي صفات المعاني قديمة بالذات أي بذاتها؛ أي إن قدمها ذاتي وليست بممكنة في نفسها، وإنما قدمها بقدم الذات المقدس، أو أن ذاته تعالى علة فيها، كما قال بذلك بعض علماء أهل السنة، وهو قول شنيع، تمجه قلوب الصالحين العارفين بربهم، إذ لا يخفى ما فيه من إساءة الأدب بمقام الله الأعز الأحمى، مع أنه لا حجة على ارتكابه، بل الحجة قائمة على ما ذكرنا، كما أشرت له بقولي: قوله: (وصلوحي قديم بذاتنا وصفاتنا): أي: قبل وجودنا. قوله: (أو أن ذاته تعالى علة فيها): (أو) بمعنى الواو; لأن هذا هو معنى قوله: وإنما قدمها بقدم الذات. قوله: (بعض علماء أهل السنة): أي: وهو الفخر الرازي، وتبعه السعد والبيضاوي وجماعة، وشنع ابن التلمساني على الفخر بقوله: لأنها ليست بغير الذات الذات العليا، أنها لا تنفك عنها، فلا يعقل قيام الذات بدونها، ولا وجودها في غير الذات المقدس، فلا يصح القول بأنها ممكنة في نفسها... ممكنة وصرح الفخر - والعياذ بالله - بكلمة لم يسبق إليها، فقال: هي باعتبار ذاتها، واجبة بوجوب ذاته جل وعلا، وضاهى قول الفلاسفة: العالم ممكن باعتبار ذاته واجب بوجوب مقتضيه، ونعوذ بالله من زلة عالم، وبناها على اعتقاد صحة شبهة الفلاسفة; بأن الافتقار بمعنى مطلق التوقف يوجب الإمكان، وأن كل مركب مفتقر إلى أجزائه، وجزؤه غيره، والمفتقر للغير لا يكون إلا ممكناً، وتوهم التركيب باعتبار الصفات، وادعى أن الإمكان لا ينافي القدم، وهي عقيدة باطلة تهدم كثيراً من مسائل أهل السنة. قوله: (لأنها ليست بغير الذات أي ولا بعينها كما يأتي، فلا يقال لها: غير الذات ولا عينها، وقصد المصنف بذلك الرد على المعتزلة، حيث أوردوا على أهل السنة شبهة حاصلها: أنكم ادعيتم وجود صفات المعاني وقد كفرتم النصارى بزيادة إلهين، فأنتم أولى في الكفر لإثبات قدماء ثمانية. وحاصل الجواب: أن المحظور المبطل للتوحيد إنما هو تعدد القدماء المتغايرة المنفكة وصفات المعاني ليست كذلك، فعلم أن مذهب أهل السنة: أن صفات الذات زائدة عليها قائمة بها، لازمة لها لزوماً لا يقبل الانفكاك، فهي دائمة الوجود، مستحيلة العدم، فهو حي بحياة، عالم بعلم، قادر بقدرة، وهكذا.
Explanation that the attributes of meanings are eternal by their essences. And all of them, i.e., the attributes of meanings, are eternal by essence, i.e., by their own essence; meaning that their eternity is intrinsic, and they are not possible in themselves, but rather their eternity is by the eternity of the sacred essence, or that His essence exalted is a cause in them, as some scholars of Ahl al-Sunna said, and it is a heinous statement that the hearts of the righteous who know their Lord abhor, for what it contains of ill-adab with the station of God the Most Mighty, the Most Supreme, is not hidden, while there is no proof for adopting it, but rather proof stands on what we mentioned, as I indicated with my saying: His saying: (and a potential eternal by our essences and attributes): i.e., before our existence. His saying: (or that His essence exalted is a cause in them): (or) is in the meaning of 'and'; because this is the meaning of his saying: but its eternity is by the eternity of the essence. His saying: (some scholars of Ahl al-Sunna): i.e., he is al-Fakhr al-Razi, followed by al-Sa'd and al-Baydawi and a group, and Ibn al-Tilimsani criticized al-Fakhr with his saying: because they are not other than the essence, the supreme essence, and they do not separate from it, so the subsisting of the essence without them is not conceivable, nor their existence in other than the sacred essence, so it is not valid to say they are possible in themselves... possible. And al-Fakhr - and we seek refuge in Allah - stated a word not preceded to, and said: they are, by their essence, necessary by the necessity of His essence - glorified and exalted -, and he paralleled the saying of the philosophers: the world is possible by its essence, necessary by the necessity of its necessitator. And we seek refuge in Allah from the slip of a scholar. And he built it on the belief in the validity of the philosophers' shubha: that need in the sense of absolute dependency requires possibility, and that every composite is dependent on its parts and its part is other than it, and the dependent on other is not except possible, and he imagined composition with respect to attributes, and claimed that possibility does not contradict eternity, and it is a false creed that destroys many issues of Ahl al-Sunna. His saying: (because they are not other than the essence), meaning nor identical to it as will come, so it is not said of them: other than the essence nor identical to it, and the author intended by that to refute the Mu'tazila, when they advanced against Ahl al-Sunna a shubha summarized: you have claimed the existence of attributes of meanings and you have declared the Christians disbelievers for adding gods, so you are more deserving of disbelief for affirming eight eternal entities. And the sum of the answer: that the prohibited that nullifies tawhid is only the multiplicity of separate, independent eternal entities, and the attributes of meanings are not like that. So it is known that the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna is that the attributes of the essence are additional to it, subsisting by it, necessary to it with a necessity that does not admit separation, so they are perpetual in existence, impossible of non-existence, so He is living by a life, knowing by a knowledge, powerful by a power, and so on.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage begins by stating that the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī) are eternal by their own essences. It explains that their eternity is intrinsic, not because they are possible in themselves, but because they exist by the eternity of the divine essence. It then mentions a deviant interpretation attributed to al-Fakhr al-Rāzī and his followers that God's essence is a cause (ʿilla) for the attributes. The commentator sharply condemns this as a grave breach of adab toward God, lacking evidence, and cites Ibn al-Tilimsānī's refutation: the attributes are not other than the essence and inseparable from it, so they cannot be described as possible in themselves. The passage then reports al-Rāzī's statement that the attributes are wajib (necessary) by God's wajib, which the commentator likens to the philosophers' claim about the world being possible in itself but necessary by its cause. This is rejected as a dangerous slip that undermines key Ahl al-Sunna doctrines. Finally, the passage addresses a Mu'tazilite shubha: if Ahl al-Sunna affirm multiple eternal attributes, they are worse than Christians who affirmed two gods. The reply is that the prohibited multiplicity is only of separate, independent eternal beings, whereas the attributes are not separate in that sense; they are additional to the essence yet inherent and inseparable. The passage concludes by summarizing the Ahl al-Sunna position: the attributes of the essence are additional to it, subsisting in it, inseparable, perpetual, and impossible of non-existence—God is living by a life, knowing by a knowledge, powerful by a power, and so forth.

قديم بالذات
علة
الفخر الرازي

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator condemn the view that God's essence is a cause (ʿilla) for the attributes?
A) Because it contradicts the Quran
B) Because it implies the attributes are possible in themselves
C) Because it is a heinous breach of adab and lacks evidence
D) Because it denies the eternity of the attributes

Key Takeaway
The attributes of meanings are eternally intrinsic to God's essence, and any view making them dependent on a cause is a grave error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says that the erroneous view is 'a heinous statement that the hearts of the righteous who know their Lord abhor.' Do you feel that abhorrence? If not, what is preventing your heart from being repulsed by a view that diminishes the majesty of God's attributes?
?
When you think of God's attributes—His knowledge, power, will—do you ever subconsciously treat them as separate 'things' that God possesses, rather than being identical with His essence? How might this subtle attitude affect your reverence in worship?
?
The lesson warns against 'ill-adab with the station of God the Most Mighty.' Where in your own understanding or speech about Allah might you be guilty of a lack of adab, even in small ways? What concrete step can you take today to correct this?

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Charge of Multiple Eternal Beings
Refutation of Mu'tazilite shubha and summary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite shubha against Ahl al-Sunna and the correct response that the attributes are not separate independent entities.

Core Idea
Multiple eternal attributes do not imply multiple gods.

The Mu'tazila argued that affirming several eternal attributes amounts to polytheism, worse than Christian trinitarianism. This lesson presents the Ahl al-Sunna response: the attributes are not separate or independent, so the charge is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite shubha
Find the accusation: 'you declared Christians disbelievers for adding gods, yet you affirm eight eternal beings'.
This is a logical consistency challenge.
2
Identify the key distinction
The response says the prohibited multiplicity is of separate, independent eternal entities. The attributes are not separate in that way.
The crucial word is 'المتغايرة المنفكة'.
3
Grasp the positive summary
The passage concludes by summarizing the Sunni position: attributes are additional to the essence, subsisting in it, inseparable, perpetual, and impossible of non-existence.
This is the standard Ash'ari position.
4
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: how does this distinction safeguard tawhid while affirming real attributes?
This connects to the core idea of the lesson.

?

Sit with the reality that His attributes are as eternal and perfect as He is—how does that change the weight of your actions?

The Eternity of the Attributes of Meaning and Refutation of al-Fakhr
Sanusi affirms the eternity of attributes and refutes al-Fakhr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attributes of meaning are considered eternal by themselves and why al-Fakhr al-Razi's view that they are possible is rejected.

Core Idea
The attributes of meaning are inseparable from Allah's essence, thus eternal, not possible.

Sanusi establishes that the attributes of meaning (sifat al-ma'ani) are eternal by themselves, meaning they are not separable from the divine essence. He then refutes al-Fakhr al-Razi's claim that these attributes are possible in themselves but necessary by God's necessity, likening it to the philosophers' error. This lesson clarifies the theological stakes of affirming the eternity of attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the opening sentence carefully: 'صفات المعاني قديمة بذاتها' – note the claim and the reasoning.
The text says 'because they are not apart from the essence.'
2
Understand the proof
The author explains that the attributes cannot exist without the essence, nor the essence without them, so they are not possible in themselves.
This refutes any notion that attributes could be contingent.
3
Examine al-Fakhr's error
Al-Fakhr claimed the attributes are possible in themselves but necessary by God's necessity – a contradiction to the author's view.
This parallels the philosophers' claim about the world.
4
Analyze the refutation
The refutation lists the flawed premises: dependence implies possibility, composition implies dependence, etc.
The author warns against such a belief destroying Sunni doctrines.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفات المعاني قديمة بذاتها لأنَّها ليست بغير الذات الذات العليَّة، أنَّها لا تنفكُ عنها، فلا بمعنى يُعقل قيامُ الذَّات بدونها، ولا وجودها في غير الذات المقدس، فلا يصح القول بأنَّها ممكنة في نفسها، ..... ممكنة وصرَّح الفخر - والعياذ بالله - بكلمة لم يسبق إليها، فقال: هي باعتبار ذاتها، واجبة بوجوب ذاته جل وعلا، وضاهى قول الفلاسفة : العالم ممكن باعتبار ذاته واجب بوجوب مقتضيه، ونعوذ بالله من زلة عالم، وبناها على اعتقاد صحة شبهة الفلاسفة؛ بأنَّ الافتقار بمعنى مطلق التّوقف يوجب الإمكان، وأنَّ كلَّ مركّب مفتقر إلى أجزائه، وجزؤه غيره، والمفتقر للغير لا يكون إلا ممكناً، وتوهم التركيب باعتبار الصفات، وادعى أنَّ الإمكان لا ينافي القدم، وهي عقيدة باطلة تهدم كثيراً من مسائل أهل السُّنَّة
The attributes of meaning are eternal by themselves, because they are not apart from the Essence—the exalted Essence—they are inseparable from it, meaning that it is not conceivable that the Essence exist without them, and they do not exist in other than the holy Essence. So it is not valid to say that they are possible in themselves... possible. And al-Fakhr—Allah's protection—explicitly stated a word unprecedented, saying: they are, in respect of their essence, necessary by the necessity of His essence, exalted. And he paralleled the philosophers' statement: the world is possible in respect of its essence and necessary by the necessity of its necessitator. And we seek refuge in Allah from the slip of a scholar. And he built it upon believing the correctness of the philosophers' sophism: that dependence in the sense of absolute need implies possibility, and that every composite is dependent upon its parts, and its part is other than it, and the dependent upon other cannot be except possible. And he imagined composition with respect to attributes, and claimed that possibility does not contradict pre-eternity. And it is a false belief that destroys many issues of Ahl al-Sunna.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof followed by a refutation. The author first states that the attributes of meaning (sifat al-ma'ani) are eternal by themselves (qadima bi-dhatiha). The reason is that they are not separate from the divine essence; they coexist inseparably. Therefore, it is wrong to consider them as contingent (mumkin) in themselves, because that would imply they could exist apart from the essence. Then the author criticizes al-Fakhr al-Razi, who claimed that these attributes are possible in themselves but necessary by God's necessity. This is likened to the philosophers' claim about the world. The author refutes this by listing the flawed premises: that absolute dependence implies contingency, that a composite depends on its parts, and that the part is other than the whole, so the dependent is possible. Al-Fakhr mistakenly imagines composition in the attributes and claims possibility is compatible with pre-eternity. The author concludes this belief is false and destroys many issues of Ahl al-Sunna.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
قديمة بذاتها
ممكنة
الفلاسفة
الافتقار
الإمكان
القدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The attributes of meaning are possible/contingent in themselves because they are distinct from the essence.
Correction: They are inseparable from the essence; hence they are eternal, not possible.

Checkpoint
What is the main error of al-Fakhr al-Razi according to this passage?
A) He denied the attributes entirely.
B) He claimed the attributes are possible in themselves.
C) He said the attributes are identical to the essence.
D) He rejected the idea of pre-eternity.

Key Takeaway
The attributes of meaning are eternal by themselves, and any claim that they are possible or contingent undermines core Sunni doctrines.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This passage shows that even a prominent scholar like al-Fakhr can slip. What safeguards do you have in your own learning to protect yourself from adopting beliefs that 'destroy many issues of Ahl al-Sunna'?
?
The author says 'we seek refuge in Allah from the slip of a scholar.' How does this humble you regarding your own understanding? Will you examine your beliefs more carefully after reading this, asking where you might be relying on flawed reasoning?

Attributes: Neither Separate nor Identical
Objection-and-answer: refuting Mu'tazili charge of multiple eternal beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Sunni position on attributes does not entail multiple eternal beings and how the Mu'tazili objection is answered.

Core Idea
Attributes are inseparable from the essence; multiplicity of attributes is not polytheism.

In this passage, the author addresses a critical objection: if Christians are condemned for adding gods, how can Muslims affirm multiple eternal attributes? The response clarifies the difference between separate independent beings and inseparable attributes. This lesson unpacks the Sunni defense of tawhid against the Mu'tazila.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully to understand the argument flow. Notice the structure: matn explanation, objection, answer, and clarification.
2
Identify the objection
Find the Mu'tazili sophism: they claim that affirming eight eternal beings (seven attributes plus essence) is worse than the Christian Trinity. Highlight this.
3
Grasp the answer
The answer distinguishes between multiple separate essences (which violate tawhid) and multiple inseparable attributes (which do not). See how the author makes this distinction.
4
Explore the Sunni position
Note that attributes are additional to the essence but inseparable. They are neither identical nor separate. Understand why the Mu'tazili view (powerful by Himself) is false.
The author says that position is fisq, not kufr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لأنَّها ليست بغير (الذات أي ولا بعينها كما يأتي، فلا يقال لها : غير الذات ولا عينها، وقصد المصنّف بذلك الرَّدَّ على المعتزلة، حيث أوردوا على أهل السُّنَّة شبهة حاصلها : أنَّكم ادعيتم وجود صفات المعاني وقد كفرتم النّصارى بزيادة إلهين، فأنتم أولى في الكفر لإثبات قدماء ثمانية . وحاصل الجواب : أن المحظور المبطل للتَّوحيد إنما هو تعدد القدماء المتغايرة المنفكّة وصفات المعاني ليست كذلك، فعلم أنَّ مذهب أهل السُّنَّة: أنَّ صفات الذات زائدة عليها قائمة بها، لازمة لها لزوماً لا يقبل الانفكاك، فهي دائمة الوجود، مستحيلة العدم، فهو حي بحياة، عالم بعلم قادر بقدرة، وهكذا. أو أنَّ الذَّات العليَّة علَّة فيها . وكما أنَّها ليست بغير الذات ليست بعينها أيضاً، وهو واضح، وإلا لزم أن تكون الذَّاتُ صفاتٍ، وأنَّ الحياة عين العلم مثلاً، وهو باطل، فبطل ما ذهب إليه المعتزلة من أنَّه تعالى قادر بذاته، وحَى بذاته، وعالم كذلك، وهكذا، لا بصفات زائدة على الذات تسمّى بالقدرة والحياة، وهكذا؛ لئلا يلزم تعدد القدماء المحال . والجواب : أنَّ المُحال إنَّما هو تعدُّد ذوات، أمَّا ذات واحدة متّصفة بصفات لا يصح الانفكاك عنها فليس بمحال، بل هو الواجب. وإنَّما اقتصرنا على الأول لأننا في مقام الاستدلال على أنَّ قدمها ذاتي. وقد نفى المعتزلة تلك الصفات هروباً من تلك الشُّبهة، وقالوا : قادر بذاته . . . إلى آخرها؛ وهو مذهب باطل، لكنَّه فسق وليس بكفر.
His statement: 'Because they are not other than the Essence' i.e., nor identical to it, as will come. So it is not said of them: other than the Essence nor identical to it. And the author intended by that to refute the Mu'tazila, where they raised against Ahl al-Sunna a sophism the sum of which is: You claim the existence of the attributes of meaning while you declared the Christians disbelievers for adding two gods, so you are more deserving of disbelief for affirming eight eternal beings. And the sum of the answer: The prohibited that nullifies tawhid is only the multiplicity of separate eternal beings, and the attributes of meaning are not like that. So it is known that the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna is that the attributes of the Essence are additional to it, subsisting by it, inseparable from it in a separation that does not admit detachment. So they are perpetual in existence, impossible of non-existence. So He is living by life, knowing by knowledge, powerful by power, and so on. Or that the exalted Essence is a cause in them. And just as they are not other than the Essence, they are not identical to it either, and that is clear. Otherwise it would necessitate that the Essence be attributes, and that life be the same as knowledge for example, and that is false. So falsified is what the Mu'tazila held: that He is powerful by Himself, living by Himself, knowing likewise, and so on, not by attributes additional to the Essence called power and life, and so on, lest the multiplicity of eternal beings (impossible) follow. And the answer: The impossible is only the multiplicity of essences. As for one essence described by attributes that cannot detach, it is not impossible, rather it is necessary. And we only limited ourselves to the first because we are in the context of proving that their pre-eternity is essential. And the Mu'tazila denied those attributes fleeing from that sophism, and said: powerful by Himself... to its end. And it is a false doctrine, but it is fisq and not kufr.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. It begins by explaining a line of the matn: 'because they are not other than the essence' meaning the attributes are neither separate from the essence nor identical to it. The purpose is to refute the Mu'tazila. The Mu'tazili objection is presented: you accuse Christians of disbelief for adding two gods (Jesus and Mary), yet you affirm eight eternal beings (the attributes), so you are worse. The author gives the answer: the prohibition is only against multiplicity of separate, independent eternal beings. The attributes are not separate; they are inseparable from the one essence. Hence it does not violate tawhid. The author then clarifies the Sunni position: the attributes are additional to the essence, subsisting in it, inseparable. Then he discusses another angle: the attributes are not identical to the essence either, because that would conflate them. The Mu'tazila's view that God is powerful by Himself (without a power attribute) is false but considered fisq (sin) not kufr (disbelief).

Key Terms

القدماء
المعتزلة
تعدد القدماء
فسق
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming multiple eternal attributes of God entails multiple gods.
Correction: The Sunni position affirms attributes that are inseparable from the essence, not separate independent beings. Multiplicity of inseparable attributes does not violate tawhid.

Checkpoint
What is the alleged 'eight eternal beings' in the Mu'tazili objection?
A) The eight names of God.
B) The seven attributes plus the essence.
C) The eight attributes of meaning.
D) The eight angels.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position on divine attributes avoids polytheism by affirming attributes that are inseparable from the essence, not separate beings.

How can you strengthen your conviction that these attributes are real yet inseparable from Him, without falling into the extremes of denial or analogy?
?
The Mu'tazila feared that affirming attributes leads to polytheism. Have you ever hesitated to affirm a divine attribute because it seemed too 'human' or 'multiple'? In what area of your faith do you struggle to trust the Sunni position over your own reasoning, and what step will you take to overcome that hesitation?
?
The passage teaches that the Mu'tazili error is fisq, not kufr. If you meet someone who holds that God is powerful only by Himself without an attribute, does this ruling make you more patient with them? How can you balance firmness in truth with mercy towards those who err, without compromising your belief?

Classification of Divine Attributes into Six Categories
Sanusi enumerates and defines six types of divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six categories of divine attributes as outlined by Sanusi, including essential, negative, active, existential, relational, and comprehensive.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are classified into six categories, each with a distinct logical relationship to the essence.

In this passage, Sanusi provides a systematic classification of the divine attributes. He organizes them into six types based on their relationship to the Essence: those identical to it, those other than it, those neither identical nor other, and comprehensive ones. This classification helps in understanding the nature of each attribute and avoids confusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to get the gist.
Notice the author's concise enumeration style.
2
Identify the six categories
The passage lists several 'or' clauses. Count them: essential, negative, active, existential, relational, comprehensive. Note that active is grouped under negative.
The author uses 'or' to introduce each category.
3
Understand the logical relationships
Distinguish between attributes identical to the Essence (essential), those other than the Essence (negative and active), those neither identical nor other (existential and relational), and comprehensive.
These distinctions are crucial for kalam reasoning.
4
Examine the textual clarification
The author comments that 'or' in the matn is used in the sense of 'and'. This clarifies that the categories are not mutually exclusive in the original text.
This shows the importance of precise language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحاصل : أنَّ الصِّفات : إما عين الذَّات النَّفسيَّة، أو غير الذات وهي السَّلبيَّة؛ لكون مدلولها عدماً والفعلية لحدوثها، أو لا عين الذات ولا غيرها وهي وجوديَّة، وتسمى المعاني، أو لا عين الذات ولا غيرها وهي اعتباريَّة، وتسمَّى معنويَّة، أو صفات جامعة وهي العزة والجلال والجمال والغنى، وغير ذلك . قوله : (أو أنَّ الذَّات ... إلخ) : (أو) بمعنى الواو كما تقدم نظيره، فكان الأوضح التّعبير بها.
And the summary: the attributes: either identical to the essential Essence, or other than the Essence and they are the negative ones, because their signification is non-existence and the active ones due to their temporality; or neither identical to the Essence nor other than it and they are existential, called al-ma'ani; or neither identical to the Essence nor other than it and they are relational, called al-ma'nawiyya; or comprehensive attributes which are might, majesty, beauty, self-sufficiency, and others. His statement: 'Or that the Essence... etc.': 'Or' is in the meaning of 'and' as its parallel has preceded, and the expression with it would have been clearer.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration and classification. The author provides a typology of divine attributes. He lists five (actually six) types: 1) Attributes that are identical to the essential Essence (sifat al-dhat al-nafsiyya), like existence. 2) Attributes that are other than the essence, i.e., negative attributes (sifat salbiyya), because their meaning is negation (e.g., not being a body). Active attributes (sifat fi'liyya) are also included in this category because they are temporal. 3) Attributes that are neither identical nor other, but existential (wujūdiyya), called attributes of meaning (sifat al-ma'ani), like life, knowledge, power. 4) Attributes that are neither identical nor other, but relational (i'tibāriyya), called attributes of meaning (sifat ma'nawiyya), like being living, knowing. 5) Comprehensive attributes (sifat jāmi'a) like might, majesty, beauty, self-sufficiency. Then he comments on a line of the matn: 'Or that the Essence...' where 'or' is used in the sense of 'and', indicating a textual clarification.

Key Terms
عين الذات
السلبية
الفعلية
الوجودية
المعاني
الاعتبارية
المعنوية
الصفات الجامعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the classification strictly separates active attributes from negative ones.
Correction: Active attributes are included under the category of 'other than the essence' along with negative ones, because both are not identical to the essence.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a category of attributes mentioned in this classification?
A) Essential attributes.
B) Negative attributes.
C) Active attributes.
D) Non-existential attributes.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi divides divine attributes into six categories: essential, negative, active, existential, relational, and comprehensive, each defined by its logical relationship to the Essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite Allah's name 'al-Ashraf' (the Most High), do you consciously reflect on whether this attribute is essential to His being or simply a description of His actions? How does Sanusi's classification challenge you to think more deeply about each attribute's relation to Allah's essence?
?
Sanusi mentions comprehensive attributes like majesty and beauty. Which of these attributes do you find yourself neglecting in your daily worship, and what concrete step will you take this week to meditate on it specifically during your supplications?
?
The passage notes that 'or' can mean 'and', showing that categories are not always exclusive. In your own understanding of Allah's oneness, do you sometimes compartmentalize His attributes incorrectly? What is one attribute you need to integrate more fully into your conviction of divine unity?

Divine Attributes and Refutation of Mu'tazila
Sawi refutes Mu'tazila on attributes and classifies types of attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutation of the Mu'tazilite position on divine attributes and the classification of attributes according to Sunni theology.

Core Idea
Attributes do not multiply essences; one essence can have many attributes.

Imam al-Sawi presents a crucial defense of divine attributes against Mu'tazilite objections. He then provides a systematic classification of the types of attributes, clarifying their relationship to the divine essence. This lesson unpacks both the argument and the taxonomy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite position
Read the opening lines describing the Mu'tazilite claim that God is powerful, knowing, etc. by His essence alone, without additional attributes. Note their fear of multiplicity of eternal entities.
2
Follow the refutation
See how the author responds: multiplicity of essences is impossible, but one essence with multiple inseparable attributes is not only possible but necessary. Identify the key distinction.
3
Learn the classification of attributes
The passage ends with a summary dividing attributes into six types. Go through each: essential, negative, active, existential, relational, and comprehensive. Understand what each means.
Use the guided breakdown for details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو أنَّ الذَّات العليَّة علَّة فيها . وكما أنَّها ليست بغير الذات ليست بعينها أيضاً، وهو واضح، وإلا لزم أن تكون الذَّاتُ صفاتٍ، وأنَّ الحياة عين العلم مثلاً، وهو باطل، فبطل ما ذهب إليه المعتزلة من أنَّه تعالى قادر بذاته، وحَى بذاته، وعالم كذلك، وهكذا، لا بصفات زائدة على الذات تسمّى بالقدرة والحياة، وهكذا ؛ لئلا يلزم تعدد القدماء المحال . والجواب : أنَّ المُحال إنَّما هو تعدُّد ذوات، أمَّا ذات واحدة متّصفة بصفات لا يصح الانفكاك عنها فليس بمحال، بل هو الواجب. وإنَّما اقتصرنا على الأول لأننا في مقام الاستدلال على أنَّ قدمها ذاتي. وهي وقد نفى المعتزلة تلك الصفات هروباً من تلك الشُّبهة، وقالوا : قادر بذاته . . . إلى آخرها ؛ وهو مذهب باطل، لكنَّه فسق وليس بكفر . والحاصل : أنَّ الصِّفات : إما عين الذات النَّفسيَّة، أو غير الذات وهي السَّلبيَّة ؛ لكون مدلولها عدماً والفعلية لحدوثها، أو لا عين الذات ولا غيرها وهي وجوديَّة، وتسمى المعاني، أو لا عين الذات ولا غيرها وهي اعتباريَّة، وتسمَّى معنويَّة، أو صفات جامعة وهي العزة والجلال والجمال والغنى، وغير ذلك . قوله : (أو أنَّ الذَّات ... إلخ) : (أو) بمعنى الواو كما تقدم نظيره، فكان الأوضح التّعبير بها .
Or that the supreme Essence is a cause in it. And just as it is not other than the Essence, it also is not identical to it, and this is clear; otherwise it would necessitate that the Essence be attributes, and that life be identical to knowledge, for example, and that is false. So what the Mu'tazila went to is refuted: that He, exalted, is powerful by His essence, living by His essence, knowing likewise, and so on, without attributes superadded to the essence called power, life, etc.; to avoid the impossible multiplicity of eternal entities. The answer: The impossible is only multiplicity of essences (dhawat). As for one essence qualified by attributes from which it cannot be separated, that is not impossible, but rather necessary. We only restricted ourselves to the first because we are in the context of proving that their eternality is essential. And they (the Mu'tazila) denied those attributes fleeing from that doubt, and said: 'Powerful by His essence...' to the end; it is a false doctrine, but it is sin (fisq) and not unbelief. The summary: Attributes are either identical to the essential essence, or other than the essence and they are negative (salbiyya) because their meaning is non-existence, and active (fi'liyya) because of their temporality, or neither identical to the essence nor other than it and they are existential (wujudiyya) and called meanings (ma'ani), or neither identical nor other and they are relational (i'tibariyya) and called abstract meanings (ma'nawiyya), or comprehensive attributes which are might, majesty, beauty, richness, and others. His saying: ('Or that the essence... etc.') : 'Or' has the meaning of 'and' (waw) as its counterpart has preceded, so expressing by it would have been clearer.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a combined refutation and classification. The author first argues against the Mu'tazilite position that God is powerful, knowing, etc. by His essence without superadded attributes. The Mu'tazila feared that admitting additional attributes would imply multiple eternal entities. The author responds that the impossibility lies in multiple independent essences, not in one essence having inherent, inseparable attributes. He then notes that the Mu'tazilite view, while false, is considered fisq (sin) not kufr (unbelief). Next, he provides a classification of attributes: (1) essential (nafsiyya) identical to the essence, (2) negative (salbiyya) indicating negation, (3) active (fi'liyya) due to temporality, (4) existential (wujudiyya) called ma'ani, (5) relational (i'tibariyya) called ma'nawiyya, and (6) comprehensive attributes. Finally, a textual note explains that the word 'aw (or) in the opening actually functions like waw (and).

وجودية (wujudiyya)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite claim that affirming multiple eternal attributes implies multiple eternal gods.
Correction: The author clarifies that it is multiplicity of independent essences that is impossible, not multiplicity of attributes in a single essence.

Checkpoint

D) It is the correct view

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position affirms multiple real attributes superadded to the divine essence without implying multiplicity of eternal entities.

How does this affect your invocation of Him in your daily life? Commit tonight to reflect on one attribute as a reality, not just a title, and let it transform your awe.

Divine Attributes

Divine Speech as an Eternal Mental Attribute
Sawi explains the Ash'ari doctrine of kalam nafsi against Mu'tazila and Karramiyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunnah distinguish between verbal and mental speech to defend God's eternal attribute of speech.

Core Idea
God's speech is an eternal mental attribute, not made of letters or sounds.

This passage addresses a key dispute about divine speech. The Mu'tazila argued that speech is composed of created letters and sounds, so God cannot possess it. Ahl al-Sunnah responded by distinguishing between verbal (created) and mental (eternal) speech. Let's examine the reasoning and see how this also refutes the Karramiyya.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite objection
The passage begins by presenting the Mu'tazilite claim that speech is only letters and sounds, which are created. They conclude that God cannot be described with speech, interpreting scriptural references as God creating speech in another.
The Mu'tazila based their argument on the impossibility of originated (created) attributes inhering in God.
2
See the Ahl al-Sunnah response
Ahl al-Sunnah refute by denying that speech is restricted to letters and sounds. They divide speech into two types: verbal (lafzi) and mental (nafsi). The mental speech is an eternal attribute of God, not composed of sounds or order.
This response removes the contradiction: God's speech is not like human speech.
3
Recognize the refutation of the Karramiyya
The author notes that his formulation also refutes the Karramiyya, who held that God's speech consists of letters and sounds but is eternal. By denying letters and sounds, the Ash'ari position avoids both errors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معنى الكلام عند أهل السنة ولمَّا ذهب المعتزلة إلى استحالة الكلام عليه تعالى، لأنَّه إنَّما يكون بحروف وأصوات، وتقديم وتأخير، وغير ذلك، وهذه كلُّها حادثة، ولا يصحُ اتصافه تعالى بالحوادث، وإلا لكان حادثاً. وصرفوا ما ورد في الكتاب والسُّنَّة، من أنَّه تعالى متكلّم، عن ظاهره على معنى أنَّه خالق الكلام في غيره ؛ كالشَّجرة التي كلمت موسى عليه السَّلام مثلاً ، فالكلام صفة غيره لا صفته تعالى. أجاب أهل السُّنَّة بمَنْع حصر الكلام في الحروف والأصوات، بجَعل الكلام قسمين: لفظي ونفسي، والثاني هو المراد، كما أشار إليه بقوله : ثمَّ الكلام أي كلامه ،تعالى الذي هو صفة ذاته، نفسي، (ليس بالحروف والأصوات، (وليس) متلبساً (بالترتيب) من تقديم وتأخير، ( كـ) الكلام الحادث (المألوف لنا، وحينئذ فلا يلزم المحال . وفي قولي: (ليس بالحروف .... إلخ ردُّ أيضاً على الكرَّاميَّة قوله : (ولما ذهب المعتزلة إلى استحالة الكلام عليه تعالى . . . إلخ) : حاصله : أنَّ المعتزلة يقولون : إنَّ الكلام لا يكون إلا حروفاً وأصواتاً، وحينئذ فلا يتصف به المولى بحيث يكون قائماً به؛ لئلا يلزم قيام الحوادث به ، ومعنى كونه متكلّماً أنَّه خالق للكلام في غيره.
The meaning of speech according to Ahl al-Sunnah. When the Mu'tazila held the impossibility of speech (kalam) for Him, exalted, because it only comes about through letters and sounds, and precedence and delay, etc., and all of these are originated (haditha), and it is not valid for Him, exalted, to be qualified by originated things, otherwise He would be originated. And they interpreted what is in the Book and Sunnah that He is speaking (mutakallim) away from its apparent meaning to mean that He is the creator of speech in another; like the tree that spoke to Moses, peace be upon him, for example, so speech is an attribute of another, not His attribute. Ahl al-Sunnah answered by preventing the restriction of speech to letters and sounds, by making speech two types: verbal (lafzi) and mental (nafsi), and the second is intended, as he indicated by his saying: 'Then speech, i.e. His speech, exalted, which is an attribute of His essence, is mental (nafsi), (not consisting of letters and sounds), and (not) connected with (order) of precedence and delay, (like) originated speech (familiar to us). Thus the impossible does not follow.' And in my saying: ('Not consisting of letters... etc.') there is also a refutation of the Karramiyya. His saying: ('When the Mu'tazila held the impossibility... etc.) : Its summary is that the Mu'tazila say that speech is nothing but letters and sounds, and then the Lord is not qualified by it with it subsisting in Him; to avoid the subsistence of originated things in Him, and the meaning of His being speaking is that He is the creator of speech in another.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage defines the Ash'ari position on divine speech (kalam). The Mu'tazila argued that speech consists of letters and sounds, which are created, so God cannot have speech as an attribute; they interpreted scriptural references to God speaking as meaning He creates speech in something else (e.g., the tree that spoke to Moses). Ahl al-Sunnah respond by distinguishing two kinds of speech: verbal (lafzi) which is created, and mental (nafsi) which is an eternal attribute of God, not composed of letters or sounds. This mental speech is what is meant when we say God is speaking. The author also notes that this refutes the Karramiyya, who apparently held that God's speech is composed of letters and sounds but is eternal. Finally, he summarizes the Mu'tazilite position for clarity.

Key Terms
كلام (kalam)
لفظي (lafzi)
نفسي (nafsi)
حروف (huruf)
أصوات (aswat)
حادثة (haditha)
مألوف (ma'luf)
كرامية (Karramiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's speech is like human speech, composed of letters and sounds.
Correction: God's speech is a mental attribute without letters or sounds.

Checkpoint
How did Ahl al-Sunnah respond to the Mu'tazilite claim that speech consists of letters and sounds?
A) They denied that God speaks
B) They accepted the Mu'tazilite interpretation
C) They distinguished between verbal and mental speech
D) They said God's speech is like human speech

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari doctrine affirms divine speech as an eternal mental attribute, distinct from created verbal speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Mu'tazila let their intellect lead them to deny God's attribute of speech. Can you identify an area in your own life where your reasoning has led you to resist or reinterpret a clear teaching from Allah? What would it take to submit fully?
?
The Karramiyya tried to affirm God's speech but compromised by mixing in human elements. Are there beliefs or practices you hold that blend truth with something comfortable or familiar to you, rather than accepting the divine reality as it is?

The Linguistic Meaning of 'ضد' in Divine Attributes
Al-Sawi defines the term 'ضد' as linguistic opposition in divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that 'ضد' in this context refers to linguistic opposition, meaning absolute incompatibility, whether existent or non-existent, and that God is free from everything that contradicts His attributes.

Core Idea
'ضد' here means absolute incompatibility—not just opposites technically.

In discussing divine attributes, the term 'ضد' can be ambiguous. Al-Sawi clarifies that in this context, 'ضد' is used in its linguistic sense, encompassing any form of incompatibility. This broad definition helps reinforce the doctrine that God is free from all contradictions to His attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own wording come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage has two parts: a definition and a commentary.
2
Identify the key definitions
Find where Al-Sawi defines 'الضّدّ اللُّغوي' (linguistic opposite) and note its two components: absolute incompatibility and the inclusion of both existent and non-existent.
3
Understand the distinction from technical opposite
Al-Sawi contrasts 'الضّدّ اللُّغوي' with 'الضد الاصطلاحي' (technical opposite). Understand that the linguistic sense is broader and more relevant to divine attributes.
The technical opposite is a narrower term in kalam/logic.
4
Examine the commentator's expansion
Read the commentary part: 'قوله : (كلُّ ما ينافي ... إلخ )'. It clarifies that 'كل ما ينافي' includes opposites in reality, contradictories, equivalents, and more specific items. List these to see the scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمراد بالضّدّ هنا الضّدُّ اللُّغوي، وهو: مطلق المنافي، سواء كان وجوديّاً أو عدميّاً، فكأنَّه قال : ويستحيل عليه تعالى كل ما ينافي ما تقدَّم من الصفات لا الضد الاصطلاحي على ما سيأتي . قوله : (كلُّ ما ينافي ... إلخ ) : أي : سواء كان ضدّاً حقيقة، أو نقيضاً أو مساوياً للنقيض أو أخص منه .
And what is meant by 'opposite' here is the linguistic opposite, which is: absolute incompatibility, whether it is existent or non-existent. So it is as if he said: It is impossible for Him, exalted is He, everything that contradicts what was mentioned of the attributes, not the technical opposite, as will come. His saying: (Everything that contradicts ... etc.): i.e., whether it is an opposite in reality, or a contradictory, or equivalent to the contradictory, or more specific than it.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a clarification of the term 'ضد' (opposite) as used in the context of divine attributes. The author specifies that here 'ضد' is meant in the linguistic sense, which encompasses absolute incompatibility, whether the incompatibility is between existent things or between existence and non-existence. The point is to assert that God is free from everything that contradicts the attributes previously mentioned, not only from those things that are technically considered 'opposites' in the terminology of kalam or logic. The commentator adds that this includes anything that is an opposite in the real sense, a contradictory, or something equivalent to or more specific than a contradictory.

Correction: In this context, 'ضد' means absolute incompatibility, covering all forms of contradiction and opposition, whether existent or non-existent.

Impossibility of Non-Existence and Origination for God
Al-Sawi deduces that thirteen attributes are impossible for God, focusing on non-existence and temporal origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why non-existence and temporal origination are impossible for God, and how these concepts relate to the negation of existence.

Core Idea
Non-existence and origination are impossible for the Necessary Being.

Al-Sawi concludes his discussion of God's necessary attributes by showing that thirteen attributes are impossible for Him, including non-existence and temporal origination. This passage clarifies the relationship between these concepts and the broader notion of the negation of existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the conclusion that thirteen attributes are impossible for God, with focus on non-existence and origination.
2
Understand the counting difference
Al-Sawi mentions that the count of thirteen depends on a specific method; if one includes the ma‘nawiyya attributes, the number becomes twenty. Reflect on why the counting matters.
This shows the internal debate among scholars on classifying attributes.
3
Examine the definitions
Focus on how al-‘adam (non-existence) and al-huduth (temporal origination) are defined. Note their relationship to the negation of existence (naqid al-wujud) and the role of the doctrine of states (al-ahwal).
4
Reflect on impossibility
Consider why these attributes are impossible for God: because God's existence is necessary (wajib) and therefore cannot accept non-existence or temporal origination.
Connect back to the earlier lesson on necessary attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اذا علمت ذلك فيستحيل عليه تعالى ثلاثة عشر صفة وهي . الصفات الأولى، لما علمت أنها واجبة له تعالى، والواجب لا يقبل الانتفاء، فيستحيل عليه تعالى : العدمُ والحدوث. قوله : (ثلاثة عشر (صفة) أي: بمقتضى ذكره للصفات كذلك، ومن عد المعنويَّة؛ كالسَّنوسي (١) ، فالمستحيلات عشرون . قوله : (العدم) : هو مساو لنقيض الوجود؛ لأن نقيضه لا وجود وهو العدم على القول بنفي الأحوال، وأما على القول بثبوتها ؛ فالعدم أخص من نقيض الوجود، إذ يصدق نقيضه بالثبوت وبالعدم. قوله: (والحدوث) : أي : الوجود بعد عدم وهو أخص من نقيض
When you know that, then it is impossible for Him, exalted, thirteen attributes, namely the first attributes, since you know that they are necessary for Him, exalted, and the necessary does not accept non-existence. Thus it is impossible for Him, exalted: non-existence (al-‘adam) and temporal origination (al-huduth). His statement: 'Thirteen attributes' meaning according to his listing of the attributes in that way, and whoever counts the ma‘nawiyya (attributes of meaning), like al-Sanusi, then the impossibilities are twenty. His statement: 'Non-existence' is equal to the negation of existence (naqid al-wujud) because its opposite is no existence, and that is non-existence according to the view that denies states (al-ahwal). But according to the view that affirms them, then non-existence is more specific than the negation of existence, since its opposite applies to both affirmation and non-existence. His statement: 'Temporal origination' means existence after non-existence, and it is more specific than the negation.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion and definition. After establishing that God's attributes are necessary, al-Sawi states that it is impossible for Him to have thirteen attributes, among them non-existence (al-‘adam) and temporal origination (al-huduth). Then he clarifies that counting thirteen depends on one method; if one counts the ma‘nawiyya (attributes of meaning), as Sanusi did, the impossible attributes become twenty. Then he defines ‘adam: it is equivalent to the negation of existence according to the view that denies states (ahwal), but if states are affirmed, then ‘adam is more specific than the negation of existence. Then he defines huduth as existence after non-existence, which is more specific than the negation of existence.

Key Terms
العدم (al-‘adam)
الحدوث (al-huduth)
نقيض الوجود (naqid al-wujud)
الأحوال (al-ahwal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Non-existence and temporal origination are identical or unrelated.
Correction: Non-existence is the absence of existence; temporal origination is existence after non-existence. They are distinct but both impossible for God.

Checkpoint

A) They are equivalent.
B) Non-existence is more specific than the negation of existence.
C) The negation of existence is more specific than non-existence.
D) There is no relation.

Key Takeaway
Non-existence and temporal origination are impossible for God, and their definitions show they are more specific than the general negation of existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God cannot cease to exist and never came into being, then He is the only permanent reality in your life. When everything around you crumbles, do you truly anchor your heart in His permanence? What one habit can you start today to live in constant awareness of His eternality?
?
The lesson defines origination as 'existence after non-existence'. If God were originated, He would not be fully worthy of worship. Have you ever, even for a moment, thought of God as coming into being or changing? What will you do when such thoughts enter your mind to reinforce His transcendence?
?
Non-existence is impossible for God, yet you will face your own non-existence. How does knowing that your Lord is eternally existent change the way you prepare for your meeting with Him? Write a concrete resolution to act on before the day ends.
