Ijad and the Two Attachments of Divine Power
Al-Sawi defines ijad and resolves the objection about power's attachment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of divine creation (ijad) as the attachment of power, and the distinction between its potential and effective attachments.

Core Idea
Creation is the effective attachment of divine power; only the potential attachment is necessary.

Al-Sawi defines ijad as the attachment of divine power to the existence of the possible. He then anticipates a confusion: if the attachment of power is necessary, how can creation be permissible? His answer distinguishes between the timeless potential attachment and the temporal effective attachment, clarifying that only the former is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of ijad
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice that ijad (bringing into existence) is defined as the attachment of divine power (qudra) to the existence of the object of power (maqdur).
Ijad and khalaq (creation) are synonyms in this context.
2
Understand the different names of attachments
The attachment of power takes different names depending on what it attaches to: life, death, provision. These attachments are the actions themselves, and they are contingent.
3
Grasp the objection
The objection states that if the attachment of power is necessary (wajib), how can creation be described as permissible (ja'iz)? Read both sides.
This is a classic kalam problem requiring precise terminology.
4
Distinguish between suluhi and tanjizi attachments
The answer resolves the contradiction: the necessary attachment is the potential (suluhi) one, which is eternal and essential. The effective (tanjizi) attachment is temporal and thus permissible. This distinction is crucial.
Memorize these two terms: al-ta‘alluq al-ṣulūḥī and al-ta‘alluq al-tanjīzī.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اتّصافه (جل) عن ذلك الافتقار (الغني)، بالسكون للوزن؛ أي: عن كل ما سواه، لاتصافه تعالى بكلِّ كمال وتنزُّهه عن كل نقص (المقتدر) على فهو إليه فقير. كل شيء، وكل ثـ ولما أنهى الكلام على قسمي الواجب والمستحيل، شرع في بيان الجائز فقال : (وجائز في حقه تعالى (الإيجاد ) أي : إيجاد الممكنات ... قوله : (أي: إيجاد الممكنات أشار بذلك إلى أنَّ (أل) عوض عن المضاف إليه . سواء وجدت بالفعل أو لم توجد . والإيجاد والخلق بمعنى واحد، وهو: تعلق القدرة بوجود المقدور، فإن تعلقت بالحياة سمي إحياء، وبالموت سمي إماتة، وبالمرزوق سمّي رزقاً وترزيقاً، وهذه التعلقات هي الأفعال، وهي حادثة كما ترى؛ لأنَّها عبارة عن التَّعلُّق التنجيزي للقدرة، وهو حادث قطعاً . المسماة بصفات فإن قلت : قد تقدَّم أنَّ تعلق القدرة واجب، فكيف يحكم عليه هنا بالجواز؟ قلتُ : الواجب التَّعلُّق الصُّلوحيُّ القديم، أمَّا التَّنجيزي فجائز، وكل جائز حادث. قوله : (قد تقدَّم أن تعلّق القدرة واجب) : أي : في قوله : وواجب تعليق ذي الصفات حتماً دواماً ما عدا الحياة . قوله : (التَّعلُّق الصُّلوحي) : أي : كونها صالحة للفعل والتّرك وهذا السُّؤال والجواب : تقييد لما تقدَّم من الإطلاق.
His description (majestic) of being free from that need (the Independent), with sukun for meter; i.e. from everything other than Him, because He is described with every perfection and free from every deficiency, the Omnipotent over everything, He is needy to Him. Everything, and every [?]. And when he finished the speech on the two divisions of the necessary and the impossible, he began to explain the permissible and said: 'And permissible in His right is bringing into existence (ijad) i.e. bringing possibles into existence...' His saying: 'i.e. bringing possibles into existence' he indicated by that that the (al) is in place of the genitive. 'Whether they exist in actuality or do not exist.' And bringing into existence and creation are one meaning, and it is: the attachment of power to the existence of the object of power. If it attaches to life it is called giving life, and to death it is called causing death, and to the provided it is called providing and provisioning. These attachments are the actions, and they are contingent as you see; because they are expressions of the effective attachment of power, which is definitely contingent. That which is called attributes. If you say: 'It has preceded that the attachment of power is necessary, so how is it judged here as permissible?' I say: 'The necessary is the potential attachment, the eternal; as for the effective, it is permissible, and everything permissible is contingent.' His saying: 'It has preceded that the attachment of power is necessary' i.e. in his saying: 'And attachment of one with attributes is necessarily eternal except for life.' His saying: 'The potential attachment' i.e. that it is suitable for action and inaction, and this question and answer is a restriction of what preceded from the absolute.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a definition and a defense of the concept of divine creation (ījād). The author begins by noting that God is described as 'al-Ghanī' (the Independent), free from all need, and is characterized by every perfection and free from every deficiency. Then he transitions to the topic of the permissible (al-jā'iz) with respect to God, which is the act of bringing possibles into existence (ījād al-mumkināt). He explains that the definite article in 'al-ījād' substitutes for the genitive construction. Then he defines creation: it is the attachment of divine power (qudra) to the existence of the object of power. Depending on what it attaches to, it is called by different names: if to life, it is iḥyā'; if to death, imāta; if to provision, rizq or tarzīq. These attachments are actions and are contingent because they are 'effective attachments' (ta'alluq tanjīzī), which are temporal. Next, an objection is raised: it was previously established that the attachment of power is necessary (wājib), so how can it be described here as permissible (jā'iz)? The answer is that what is necessary is the 'potential attachment' (al-ta'alluq al-ṣulūḥī), which is eternal; the effective attachment is contingent and therefore permissible. The author then comments on the source text, explaining that the statement 'the attachment of power is necessary' refers to the potential attachment, i.e., that power is essentially fit to act or refrain. This distinction restricts the earlier absolute statement, clarifying that only the timeless suitability is necessary, not the actual temporal act.

Key Terms
الإيجاد
الخلق
تعلق القدرة
التعلق التنجيزي
التعلق الصلوحي
الجائز
الواجب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all attachments of divine power are necessary and eternal, conflating the potential attachment with the effective attachment.
Correction: Only the potential attachment (ṣulūḥī) is necessary and eternal; the effective attachment (tanjīzī) is permissible and contingent.

Checkpoint

A) The effective attachment (al-ta'alluq al-tanjīzī)
B) The potential attachment (al-ta'alluq al-ṣulūḥī)
C) The attachment to life
D) The attachment to death

Key Takeaway
Divine creation is the temporal effective attachment of power, not the eternal potential attachment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God's effective attachment brings everything into being at the exact moment He wills, what keeps you from surrendering your control over the outcome of your own plans today? Will you verbally affirm that His timing is perfect, even for your current uncertainty?
?
The passage distinguishes between power being 'suitable' (potential) and 'actual' (effective). In your life, you know God's power is sufficient to forgive you (potential), but do you doubt that He will actually forgive you (effective) for that sin you keep repeating? What step will you take today to sincerely repent and trust in His actual forgiveness?
?
All divine actions (including your provision and life) are contingent on His power's effective attachment—they are not automatic. How does this truth expose your ingratitude for the simple fact that you are alive and breathing right now? Pause and thank Him for each of these attachments as acts of His specific will.

Creation as Attachment of Power: Essential vs. Actual
Definition of creation as attachment of power and distinguishing essential from actual attachment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine creation is defined as the attachment of power to the existence of a possible thing, and that this attachment has two aspects: an eternal essential capacity and a contingent actual act.

Core Idea
Creation is the attachment of divine power to existence — essential forever, actual only when He wills.

Al-Sawi begins by equating 'creation' and 'bringing into existence' as the attachment of divine power to the object of power. He then distinguishes between the eternal capacity to create and the moment-by-moment decision to create. This passage solves an apparent contradiction by introducing two kinds of divine attachment.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of creation
Read the first part where creation is defined as the attachment of power to existence. Notice how it takes different names depending on what it brings about.
Power (qudra) attaches to the possible thing (maqdur).
2
Identify the two kinds of attachment
Look for the objection that says attachment of power is necessary, yet here it is called contingent. See how the commentary answers by distinguishing essential and actual attachment.
This is a key distinction in Islamic theology.
3
Understand the answer to the second objection
The text addresses a further worry about re-creating something that already exists. Understand the reply that creation considers the possible in itself.
This clarifies that creation is not redundant.
4
Review the technical terms
Make sure you understand terms like tanzizi, saluhi, ta'alluq, and haadith.
These terms are foundational for later discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سواء وجدت بالفعل أو لم توجد . والإيجاد والخلق بمعنى واحد، وهو: تعلق القدرة بوجود المقدور، فإن تعلقت بالحياة سمي إحياء، وبالموت سمي إماتة، وبالمرزوق سمّي رزقاً وترزيقاً، وهذه التعلقات هي الأفعال، وهي حادثة كما ترى؛ لأنَّها عبارة عن التَّعلُّق التنجيزي للقدرة، وهو حادث قطعاً .

فإن قلت : قد تقدَّم أنَّ تعلق القدرة واجب، فكيف يحكم عليه هنا بالجواز؟
قلتُ : الواجب التَّعلُّق الصُّلوحيُّ القديم، أمَّا التَّنجيزي فجائز، وكل جائز حادث.

قوله : (سواء وجدت بالفعل... إلخ): إن قلت : إنَّها إذا وجدت بالفعل كان واجباً لا جائزاً، وإيجاده ثانياً تحصيل حاصل؟
أجيب بأنَّ المراد إيجاد الممكن في حد ذاته بقطع النظر عن كونه موجوداً أو لا .

قوله : (وبالمرزوق) : أي : بالشَّيء المرزوق، وكان الأوضح أن يقول: وبالمرزوق به.

قوله : (قد تقدَّم أن تعلّق القدرة واجب) : أي : في قوله :
وواجب تعليق ذي الصفات حتماً دواماً ما عدا الحياة قوله : (التَّعلُّق الصُّلوحي) : أي : كونها صالحة للفعل والتّرك وهذا السُّؤال والجواب : تقييد لما تقدَّم من الإطلاق.
Whether it exists actually or not. And 'bringing into existence' (ijad) and 'creation' (khalq) are one meaning, namely: the attachment (ta'alluq) of power (qudra) to the existence of the object of power (maqdur). If it attaches to life, it is called giving life (ihya'); to death, it is called causing death (imata); to the provision (marzuq), it is called provision (rizq) and providing (tarziq). These attachments are the acts (af'al), and they are originated (haditha) as you see; because they are the actual (tanzizi) attachment of power, and it is definitely originated.

If you say: 'It has previously been established that the attachment of power is necessary (wajib), so how is it judged here as contingent (ja'iz)?' I say: 'The necessary is the essential (saluhi) eternal attachment; as for the actual (tanzizi), it is contingent, and every contingent is originated.'

His statement: 'Whether it exists actually... etc.': If you say: 'If it actually exists, then it is necessary, not contingent, and bringing it into existence a second time would be a reaccomplishing of the already accomplished (tahsil hasil).' The answer: 'What is meant is the bringing into existence of the possible in itself, regardless of whether it exists or not.'

His statement: 'And by the provision (bi al-marzuq)': i.e., by the thing that is provided. It would have been clearer to say: 'and by that which is provided'.

His statement: 'It has previously been established that the attachment of power is necessary': i.e., in his saying: 'And the attachment of the Possessor of attributes is necessarily eternal continuously except for life.' His statement: 'The essential attachment (al-ta'alluq al-saluhi)': i.e., its being suitable for doing and leaving. And this question and answer are a restriction (taqyid) of what was previously stated absolutely.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-objection discussion. It begins by defining 'creation' (khalq) and 'bringing into existence' (ijad) as the attachment (ta'alluq) of divine power (qudra) to the existence of a possible thing. This attachment, when specified to a particular effect, takes different names: giving life, causing death, providing sustenance. All such attachments are called acts (af'al) and are originated (haditha) because they are the actual (tanzizi) attachment of power, which is definitely temporal. 

An objection arises: it was previously stated that the attachment of power is necessary (wajib), so how can it be contingent here? The answer distinguishes two types of attachment: the essential (saluhi) attachment, which is the eternal suitability of power to act or refrain, and the actual (tanzizi) attachment, which is the specific determination to create a particular thing at a particular time. The former is necessary and eternal; the latter is contingent and originated. This solves the apparent contradiction.

A further question: if the thing already exists, then its creation is necessary and a second creation would be redundant (tahsil hasil). The reply clarifies that 'bringing into existence' here means considering the possible thing in itself, abstracted from its actual existence. The commentary then explains a minor wording issue (using 'marzuq' vs. 'marzuq bihi') and concludes by linking the objection and answer to the original text, showing that they restrict a previously absolute statement about the necessity of attachment.

Key Terms
القدرة (qudra)
التعلق (ta'alluq)
التنجيزي (tanzizi)
الصولحي (saluhi)
الحوادث (hawadith)
الإيجاد (ijad)
المقدور (maqdur)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that every attachment of divine power is necessary and eternal.
Correction: In fact, only the essential capacity (saluhi) is necessary and eternal; the actual act (tanzizi) is contingent and originated.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Sawi, what is the difference between the essential (saluhi) attachment of power and the actual (tanzizi) attachment?
A) The essential is contingent, the actual is necessary
B) The essential is eternal and necessary, the actual is originated and contingent
C) The essential is originated, the actual is eternal
D) Both are equally necessary

Key Takeaway
Creation is the attachment of divine power to existence: the capacity is eternal, but the act itself is contingent and originated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray for provision, do you primarily rely on God's eternal capacity to provide, or on the actual act of provision you hope to see? Which perspective makes you more patient and trusting?
?
The passage teaches that every actual attachment of power (every act of God) is newly originated. How does this truth affect your sense of God's nearness in each moment—do you live as if each breath is a new creation from Him?
?
If God's essential power is eternal and His actual acts are contingent on His will, then nothing in your life happens by accident. What would change in your heart if you fully accepted that every event today is a direct, fresh attachment of His power?

Refuting Accidents in God and the Contingency of Divine Actions
Al-Sawi responds to the objection about accidents in God and explains the contingency of all divine actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why describing Allah with originated attributes like creation does not imply change or accidents in His essence, and that all divine actions are contingent—neither obligatory nor impossible.

Core Idea
God's attributes of action are mental considerations, not real accidents; divine actions are purely contingent.

Al-Sawi addresses a key objection: if creation is an attribute of God, doesn't that imply God is subject to change and accidents? He clarifies that such attributes are mere mental considerations (umur i'tibariyya), not real qualities inhering in His essence. He then affirms that all divine actions, such as sending messengers and rewarding or punishing, are contingent—neither obligatory nor impossible—and refutes the Mu'tazila and philosophers who held extreme views.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the opening objection: how can God be described with originated things (hawadith) like creation? Then read Al-Sawi's answer: these are mental considerations with no external existence.
Notice that the answer distinguishes between existential accidents and mental attributions.
2
Understand 'mental considerations' (umur i'tibariyya)
Focus on the concept: mental considerations are relational notions like 'before' and 'after' that have no reality in themselves. They do not inhere in God's essence.
Contrast with existential accidents (e.g., whiteness) that would imply change.
3
See the application to divine actions
The passage then gives examples: sending messengers, seeing God (ru'ya), rewarding the disobedient, punishing the obedient. All are contingent—God may do or leave them.
This refutes both those who claim obligation (Mu'tazila) and those who claim impossibility (philosophers).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : الخلق والإيجاد من صفاته تعالى، وكيف يتّصف تعالى بالحوادث؟
قلنا : هذه أمور اعتبارية تعرض للقدرة لا وجود لها في الأذهان، ولا تحقق لها في نفسها، ككونه قبل العالم ومعه وبعده، فلا يلزم قيام الحوادث به تعالى.

( والتّركُ) أي : ترك الإيجاد للمكنات، سواء وجدت أو لم توجد؛ يعني : أنّ إيجاد كلِّ ممكن أو تَرْكَه أمر جائز في حقه تعالى، إن شاء فعل وإن شاء ترك، ومن ذلك : بعثةُ الرُّسُل عليهم الصَّلاة والسَّلام، ورؤية الباري تعالى وإثابة العاصي، وتعذيب المطيع.

قوله : فلا يلزم قيام الحوادث به (تعالى :أي ولا يلزم قيام الحوادث ،بذاته، إلَّا إذا كانت تلك الصفات الحادثة المتّصف بها وجوديَّة؛ كالبياض والسَّواد ،ونحوهما وأمَّا إذا كانت الصفات الحادثة المتّصف بها اعتباريَّة، ولا وجود لها في الخارج ولا ثبوت؛ فلا يلزم قيام الحوادث بذاته؛ لأنَّ الأمر العدمي الاعتباري لا يقوم بشيء.

قوله : (ومن ذلك : بعثة الرُّسل ... إلخ) : ردَّ بذلك على المعتزلة القائلين بوجوب ،بعثتهم والحكماء القائمين باستحالتها .

قوله : ( ورؤية الباري : ردَّ به على المعتزلة القائلين بأنها محالة
If you say: 'Creation and bringing into existence are among His attributes, may He be exalted, and how can He be described with originated things (hawadith)?' We say: 'These are mental considerations (umur i'tibariyya) that occur to power, having no existence in minds nor reality in themselves, like His being before the world, with it, and after it. So the occurrence of originated things in Him, may He be exalted, does not follow.'

(And leaving [al-tark]) i.e., leaving the bringing into existence of possible things, whether they exist or not; meaning that the bringing into existence of every possible thing or its leaving is a contingent matter in His right, may He be exalted: if He wills He does, and if He wills He leaves. Among that are: sending the messengers (peace and blessings be upon them), seeing the Eternal, rewarding the disobedient, and punishing the obedient.

His statement: 'So the occurrence of originated things in Him does not follow' (may He be exalted): i.e., and the occurrence of originated things in His essence does not follow, unless those originated attributes ascribed to Him are existential (wujudiyya), like whiteness and blackness and the like. But if the originated attributes ascribed to Him are mental considerations (i'tibariyya), having no existence or reality in the external world, then the occurrence of originated things in His essence does not follow, because a non-existential (adami) consideration does not inhere in anything.

His statement: 'And among that: sending the messengers... etc.': He refutes by that the Mu'tazila who assert the necessity of sending them, and the philosophers (hukama') who assert its impossibility.

His statement: 'And seeing the Eternal': He refutes by that the Mu'tazila who assert it is impossible.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer followed by doctrinal elaboration. The objection asks: if creating is an attribute of God, how can He be described by originated things (hawadith), since that would imply change in His essence? The answer is that these attributes are not real accidents inhering in God, but mental considerations (umur i'tibariyya) that attach to power conceptually, like the relative notions 'before', 'with', and 'after' the world. Such considerations have no actual existence, so they do not imply that God Himself undergoes change.

The text then discusses the concept of 'leaving' (tark) i.e., refraining from bringing a possible thing into existence. This, like the act of creation, is purely contingent in God: He may do it or not. Examples include sending messengers, seeing God (ru'ya), rewarding the disobedient, and punishing the obedient — all are within His power and not obligatory or impossible.

The commentary further clarifies: the occurrence of originated things in God would only be implied if the attributed descriptions were existential (wujudiyya), like accidents inhering in bodies. But since they are mental (i'tibariyya) and non-existent in externals, no inherence occurs. Finally, the passage refutes two groups: the Mu'tazila who assert that sending messengers is obligatory upon God, and the philosophers (hukama') who assert it is impossible. Similarly, the vision of God (ru'ya) is asserted against the Mu'tazila who deny its possibility.

الحوادث (hawadith)
أمور اعتبارية (umur i'tibariyya)
التعلق (ta'alluq)
الترك (tark)
بعثة الرسل (ba'that al-rusul)
رؤية الباري (ru'yat al-Bari)
المعتزلة (Mu'tazila)
الحكماء (hukama')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's attributes of action (like creation) are real accidents inhering in His essence, implying change.
Correction: These attributes are mental considerations (umur i'tibariyya) with no external existence; thus they do not imply accidents in God.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Sawi, why does describing God with 'originated things' (like creation) not imply that accidents inhere in His essence?
A) Because creation is not a real attribute of God
B) Because these are mental considerations with no external existence
C) Because God is above all attributes
D) Because creation is necessary, not originated

Key Takeaway
The passage defends divine transcendence by distinguishing real accidents from mere mental attributions, and affirms that all divine actions are contingent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face hardship or unanswered prayers, do you ever feel that God 'owes' you relief because of your faith or deeds? How does the truth that all divine actions are purely contingent—He may do or not do—reshape your trust and patience? What specific expectation will you surrender to Him today?
?
The passage refutes those who claim God must send messengers or must not. Have you ever insisted that God should act a certain way in your life (e.g., heal a loved one, provide a job)? What does this teach you about the difference between hope and demand? Can you turn one of your demands into a pure plea today?
?
This lesson distinguishes real accidents from mental considerations. Are you prone to think of God's actions as if they were like human actions that imply change? How might your awe of God grow when you realize He is not subject to the limitations of created attributes? Write down one way you will speak of God's actions with greater reverence starting now.

Causing misery and happiness in Ash'ari thought: temporal attributes of actions
Al-Sawi states the agreement and then explains Ash'ari view on ishqa/is'ad as temporal attributes of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Ash'ari considers ishqa' and is'ad to be temporal attributes of actions and how they relate to the connection of divine power.

Core Idea
Ishqa' and is'ad are temporal actions, not eternal attributes.

Al-Sawi begins by establishing that there is agreement that causing misery and happiness do not change. He then explains the Ash'ari position: these are attributes of actions (sifat al-af'al) which are temporal because they involve a connection of power to a determined object at the moment of action. This lesson unpacks the Ash'ari reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari passage
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the Ash'ari view. Identify the key terms: ishqa', is'ad, attributes of actions, temporal, connection of power.
2
Understand the reasoning
Al-Ash'ari identifies ishqa' and is'ad with causing death upon misery or happiness. They are attributes of actions, which are temporal because they are expressions of the connection of power (qudra) to the determined object at the time of action.
The commentary clarifies that 'connection of power' means the effective temporal connection.
3
Contrast with the eternal view
Note that this Ash'ari view is contrasted with the Maturidi view in the next lesson. For now, focus on why these attributes are temporal in Ash'ari theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإشقاء والإسعاد : فلا يتبدلان اتفاقاً :
- أما عند إمامنا الأشعري فلأنَّهما الإماتة على الشَّقاوة أو السعادة، فهما من صفات الأفعال، وهي عنده حادثة؛ لأنَّها عبارة عن تعلُّق القدرة بالمقدور ، كما مرّ .
قوله : (عبارة عن تعلق القدرة) : أي : التنجيزي الحادث.
- وأما عند الماتُريدي: فلأنَّهما قديمان؛ كالإحياء والإماتة والخلق والرّزق، وجميع ما نعبر عنه بصفات الأفعال فقد جزم الماتريدية بقدمها، ومجموعها عند محققيهم: عبارة عن صفة واحدة تسمَّى بالتَّكوين قائمة بذاته تعالى لكونها صفة معنى؛ كالقدرة والإرادة، يتأتى بها وجود الأشياء على وفق الإرادة.
As for causing misery and causing happiness: they do not change by agreement. - As for according to our master al-Ash'ari, because they are causing death upon misery or happiness, so they are from the attributes of actions, and they are in his view temporal; because they are an expression of the connection of power to the determined object, as has passed. His saying: (an expression of the connection of power): meaning the effective temporal connection. - And as for according to al-Maturidi: because they are eternal; like giving life and causing death and creation and provision, and all that we express as attributes of actions, the Maturidis have asserted their eternity, and their totality according to their verified scholars: is an expression of one attribute called origination subsisting in His essence, exalted, because it is an attribute of meaning; like power and will, by which the existence of things occurs in accordance with will.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage addresses the terms ishqa' (causing misery) and is'ad (causing happiness) which are distinct from happiness and misery themselves. Al-Sawi states that there is complete agreement among the schools that these actions on God's part do not change. He then explains the underlying reasoning for each school. For al-Ash'ari, ishqa' and is'ad are identified with causing death upon misery or happiness respectively. They belong to the category of attributes of actions (sifat al-af'al), which al-Ash'ari considers temporal (haditha) because they involve a connection of power (qudra) to a determined object at the moment of action. For al-Maturidi, these attributes are eternal because all attributes of actions are eternal in God's essence. The Maturidis reduce all such attributes to a single eternal attribute called takwin (origination), which is a real attribute of meaning (sifat ma'na) like power and will, through which things come into existence in accordance with His will.

Key Terms
الإشقاء
الإسعاد
صفات الأفعال
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Ash'aris consider ishqa' and is'ad to be temporal?
A) Because they are actions.
B) Because they involve a temporal connection of power.
C) Because they are created.
D) Because they change.

Key Takeaway
For Ash'aris, causing misery and happiness are temporal acts of God, not eternal attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that God's causing you to die in misery or happiness is a temporal act that does not change. Are you living today as if your final state is already sealed, or are you actively seeking God's mercy to die in happiness? What specific change can you make right now to incline your final end toward happiness?
?
If you truly believed that your deathbed state is directly caused by God at that moment, not merely by your past deeds, would you fear that moment less or more? Does this thought drive you to rely solely on God's grace, or does it lead you to despair?
?
The scholars agree that ishqa and is'ad do not change—once decreed, they are fixed. How does that truth sit with your longing for God's forgiveness? Does it make you more earnest in your supplications, or does it tempt you to complacency? Commit to one prayer today asking God for a happy end.

Causing misery and happiness in Maturidi thought: eternal attributes and takwin
Al-Sawi explains the Maturidi view that ishqa' and is'ad are eternal attributes, akin to takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Maturidi considers ishqa' and is'ad to be eternal attributes and how they relate to the single attribute of takwin (origination).

Core Idea
For Maturidis, ishqa' and is'ad are eternal because all attributes of actions are reduced to one eternal attribute: takwin.

Al-Sawi then explains the Maturidi position: in contrast to the Ash'ari view, the Maturidis hold that ishqa' and is'ad are eternal attributes, like all attributes of actions. The verified scholars among them reduce all such attributes to a single eternal attribute called takwin (origination), which subsists in God's essence like power and will. This lesson examines this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Maturidi passage
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the Maturidi view. Notice how it contrasts with the Ash'ari view: ishqa' and is'ad are eternal.
2
Understand the Maturidi reasoning
Al-Maturidi considers ishqa' and is'ad eternal, like giving life, causing death, creation, and provision. All attributes of actions are eternal, and their totality is one attribute called takwin, which is an attribute of meaning like power and will.
Takwin is the attribute through which things come into existence in accordance with God's will.
3
Compare with Ash'ari view
Compare this with the Ash'ari view: Ash'aris see these as temporal actions, while Maturidis see them as manifestations of an eternal attribute.

The Distinction Between Power and Origination in Maturidi Kalam
Al-Sawi distinguishes qudra from takwin and explains why takwin is needed as a separate attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi theologians distinguish between the attribute of power (qudra) and the attribute of origination (takwin), and how this distinction is grounded in the nature of their effects.

Core Idea
Power enables; origination creates.

This lesson unpacks a key Maturidi distinction: the difference between Allah's power (qudra) and His attribute of bringing things into existence (takwin). Al-Sawi explains that power only makes action possible, while takwin is the direct source of existence. We will see why this distinction is necessary and how it relates to the broader landscape of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice that al-Sawi begins by defining both terms.
2
Analyze the core distinction
Identify how al-Sawi defines qudra as 'validity of effect' and takwin as 'existence of things'. Understand why power cannot be the source of existence because it relates equally to action and omission.
This is the heart of the Maturidi position.
3
Recognize the implications for attribute counting
Notice the gloss that takwin is an attribute of meaning, making eight such attributes for Maturidis versus seven for Ash'aris. Reflect on why this difference matters.
The verse 'Be, and it is' is cited in support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرق بين صفتي القدرة والتكوين
والفرق بينها وبين القدرة: أنَّ القدرة عندهم بها صحةُ التَّأثير في الممكن، والتكوين به وجود الأشياء.
و حاصله : أنَّه لا يصح أن يكون مبدأ الوجود القدرة؛ لأنَّ أثرها صحة الفعل والتَّرْك من الفاعل، فتكون نسبتها إلى الطرفين على السَّواء، فلا بدَّ من صفة أخرى بها الصُّدور – وهي - التَّكوين – فهي ليست التّعلُّق التنجيزي للقدرة حتّى تكون حادثة وجائزة، والجائز إنَّما هو الحدوث وعدمه،
قوله : (لكونها صفة معنى؛ كالقدرة والإرادة) : أي : فتكون المعاني عنده ثمانية، وعند الأشعري سبعة .
قوله: (وهي التَّكوين) أي: المشار إليها بقوله تعالى: (كُن فَيَكُونُ (1) .
قوله : (إنَّما هو الحدوث أي : الذي هو أثر الإحداث، فالإحداث
The difference between the two attributes of power and origination. And the difference between it (origination) and power: that power according to them is that by which there is the validity of effect in the possible, and origination is that by which there is the existence of things. And its summary: that it is not valid for power to be the principle of existence; because its effect is the validity of action and omission from the agent, so its relation to the two sides is equal. Therefore, there must be another attribute by which there is issuance – and it is origination – so it is not the effective connection of power such that it is temporal and contingent, and the contingent is only temporality and its absence. His saying: (because it is an attribute of meaning; like power and will): meaning that the attributes of meaning according to him are eight, and according to al-Ash'ari seven. His saying: (and it is origination): meaning that which is indicated by His saying, exalted: 'Be, and it is.' (Quran 2:117). His saying: (only temporality): meaning that which is the effect of bringing into existence, so bringing into existence...
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage explains the Maturidi distinction between the attribute of power (qudra) and the attribute of origination (takwin). Al-Sawi first states the difference: power provides the ability (sihhat al-ta'thir) to bring about a possibility, while takwin actually gives existence. He then summarizes that power cannot be the source of existence because its effect is merely the validity of either doing or omitting an action – it is equally related to both possibilities. Therefore, a separate attribute, takwin, is needed for the actual issuance of things. This takwin is not the same as the temporal connection of power, which would make it contingent and subject to existence or non-existence. The glosses then add: takwin is an attribute of meaning (sifat ma'na) like power and will, and according to the Maturidis, the total number of such attributes is eight, whereas the Ash'aris count seven. The gloss also cites the Quranic verse 'Be, and it is' as evidence for takwin. The final gloss begins to explain that the contingent thing is temporality itself, the effect of bringing into existence.

القدرة
التكوين
صفة معنى
التأثير
الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Allah's power directly brings things into existence.
Correction: Al-Sawi clarifies that power only grants the validity of action and omission; actual existence requires a separate attribute, takwin.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is power not sufficient as the source of existence?
A) Because power is too weak.
B) Because power relates equally to action and omission.
C) Because power is created.
D) Because power is temporal.

Key Takeaway
Takwin is the attribute that brings things into existence, distinct from qudra which only grants the capacity to act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's power only provides validity but not existence, does that weaken your reliance on His ability to create? How does knowing that takwin is a distinct attribute deepen your trust in Allah's creative act?
?
Why do you often attribute creation solely to Allah's power? How can you remind yourself that His takwin is what actually brings things into being?
?
The Maturidis added takwin to the attributes to preserve the distinction between ability and action. Does your own understanding of Allah's attributes reflect careful study, or have you been content with vague concepts? What will you do to know Allah better?

The Maturidi Doctrine of Takwin and Its Distinction from Qudra
Al-Sawi explains the Maturidi view of takwin as an eternal attribute and its difference from qudra.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that takwin is an eternal attribute of meaning distinct from qudra, and why this distinction is necessary.

Core Idea
Takwin is the attribute that brings existence; qudra only enables it.

Al-Sawi clarifies a crucial point in Maturidi theology: the attribute of takwin (origination) is eternal and distinct from qudra (power). While qudra gives the ability to act, takwin directly produces existence. This distinction answers the objection that power alone cannot account for creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage uses a very compact argumentative style.
2
Identify the two attributes
Find how takwin and qudra are defined and differentiated. Qudra is described as enabling effect, while takwin brings things into existence.
The passage explicitly states that qudra relates equally to action and omission.
3
Understand the proof
Why cannot qudra be the principle of existence? Because its effect is the validity of action and abandonment, so it cannot directly produce existence. Another attribute (takwin) is needed.
This is a core logical argument for the distinction.
4
Grasp the implications
The eternity of takwin does not imply the eternity of the originated things. The passage also clarifies that temporality (hadath) is the effect of bringing-into-being, not existence itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عند الماتُريدي: فلأنَّهما قديمان؛ كالإحياء والإماتة والخلق والرّزق، وجميع ما نعبر عنه بصفات الأفعال فقد جزم الماتريدية بقدمها، ومجموعها عند محققيهم: عبارة عن صفة واحدة تسمَّى بالتَّكوين قائمة بذاته تعالى لكونها صفة معنى؛ كالقدرة والإرادة، يتأتى بها وجود الأشياء على وفق الإرادة. والفرق بينها وبين القدرة: أنَّ القدرة عندهم بها صحةُ التَّأثير في الممكن، والتكوين به وجود الأشياء. وحاصله: أنَّه لا يصح أن يكون مبدأ الوجود القدرة؛ لأنَّ أثرها صحة الفعل والتَّرْك من الفاعل، فتكون نسبتها إلى الطرفين على السَّواء، فلا بدَّ من صفة أخرى بها الصُّدور – وهي التكوين – فهي ليست التّعلُّق التنجيزي للقدرة حتّى تكون حادثة وجائزة، والجائز إنَّما هو الحدوث وعدمه. قوله: (لكونها صفة معنى؛ كالقدرة والإرادة): أي: فتكون المعاني عنده ثمانية، وعند الأشعري سبعة. قوله: (وهي التَّكوين) أي: المشار إليها بقوله تعالى: (كُن فَيَكُونُ). قوله: (إنَّما هو الحدوث أي: الذي هو أثر الإحداث، فالإحداث لا الإيجاد فإنه قديم، يتبدّلان لِقِدَمِهِما، لما علمت أنَّهما يرجعان إلى التكوين، الذي هو صفة ذاته تعالى، والشَّقاوة والسَّعادة يتبدّلان لأنهما الكفر والإيمان لا بقيد الموت على ذلك. لكونه صفة ذاته تعالى، فالإشقاء والإسعاد لا، ولا يلزم من قِدَم التَّكوين قِدَمُ المكوّن، إذ لا يلزم من قِدَم الصفة قِدَمُ متعلّقها.
And as for the Maturidi: because they are both eternal, like giving life, causing death, creating, providing, and all that we express as attributes of acts—the Maturidis have decisively stated their eternity. Their totality according to their verifiers is an expression of a single attribute called takwin (origination) subsisting in His essence, exalted, because it is an attribute of meaning, like power and will. By it the existence of things comes about in accordance with will. The difference between it and power is that power according to them is that which contains the validity of effect in the possible, while takwin is that through which things exist. The summary is that it is not valid for power to be the principle of existence, because its effect is the validity of action and abandonment from the agent, so its relation to both sides is equal. Therefore there must be another attribute by which is the emanation—and it is takwin. So it is not the actual connection of power so that it would be temporal and contingent. The contingent is only temporality and its absence. His saying: (because it is an attribute of meaning, like power and will): meaning the attributes of meaning according to him are eight, and according to al-Ash'ari are seven. His saying: (and it is takwin): meaning that which is referred to by His saying, exalted: 'Be, and it is.' His saying: (only temporality): meaning that which is the effect of bringing-into-being, so bringing-into-being is not existence, for it is eternal, they change due to their eternity, since you know that they both revert to takwin, which is an attribute of His essence. Happiness and misery change because they are disbelief and faith not conditioned by death upon that. Because it is an attribute of His essence, so causing happiness and causing misery do not. And it does not follow from the eternity of takwin the eternity of the originated thing, because the eternity of the attribute does not necessitate the eternity of its object of relation.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage defines the Maturidi position on takwin and distinguishes it from qudra. The author first states the Maturidi view that attributes like giving life, causing death, etc., are eternal and collectively called takwin. Then he explains the difference: qudra gives the ability to act or not, while takwin brings existence. The proof: power cannot directly cause existence because it relates equally to action and omission, so another attribute is needed. The commentary explains that Maturidis count eight attributes of meaning, while Ash'aris count seven. The takwin attribute is referenced in the Qur'anic 'Be'. The author also clarifies that temporality (hadath) is the effect of bringing-into-being, not existence itself, and that happiness and misery (faith and disbelief) change because they are not conditioned by death. Finally, the eternity of takwin does not imply the eternity of its objects.

Ash'ari and Maturidi on Attributes of Acts
Al-Sawi contrasts Ash'ari and Maturidi positions on attributes of acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key difference between Ash'ari and Maturidi views on the attributes of God's acts, and the Maturidi concept of takwin.

Core Idea
For Maturidis, all active attributes are one eternal attribute: takwin.

In this passage, al-Sawi summarizes a major theological debate between the Ash'aris and Maturidis. The question is whether attributes like creating, giving life, and providing are temporal or eternal. This passage lays out both positions and explains the Maturidi concept of takwin, the single eternal attribute behind all creative acts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the two groups mentioned: Ash'aris and Maturidis.
The passage begins with a list of act-attributes.
2
Identify the Ash'ari position
According to the Ash'aris, attributes like creating and providing are temporal. Why? Because they are mere relations between eternal power and temporal objects.
They are not eternal in themselves.
3
Identify the Maturidi position
According to the Maturidis, these attributes are eternal because they are aspects of one eternal attribute called takwin.
The names change based on the object (e.g., creating, causing death).
4
Understand the roles of will, power, and takwin
Will specifies, power enables (receptivity), and takwin is the actual emanation. This distinction is key to the Maturidi view.
Power is equal regarding doing or leaving; takwin is the principle of existence.
5
Reflect on the depth
Consider why this distinction matters: it preserves God's eternal activity without temporal change.
The Maturidi view maintains that God is eternally creative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجملة القول في ذلك: أنَّ الإيجاد والخلق والرزق والإحياء والإماتة والإشقاء والإسعاد والتَّصوير إلى غير ذلك عند الأشعرية صفات حادثة؛ لأنَّها إضافات واعتبارات بين القدرة والمقدور. وعند الماتريدية قديمة؛ لأنَّها صفة أزليَّة بها صدور العالم، وكلّ جزء من أجزائه، ويسمى تكويناً، لكن إن تعلقت بوجود الشَّيء سميت إيجاداً وخلقاً، أو بموته سمّيت إماتة، أو بصورته سميت تصويراً، وهي زائدة على القدرة والإرادة، فالإرادة بها التَّخصيص، والقدرة هي القوَّة على فعل الشَّيء أو تركه، ونسبة الأمرين إليها على السواء، فليس بها صدور الأشياء، وإنَّما بها قبول الصُّدور، فهي مبدأ لقبول الصُّدور، والتكوين مبدأ لنفس الصُّدور. عنده قديم والحدوث حادث. قوله: (لكن إن تعلقت ... إلخ)؛ أي: فتسمى باسم متعلقها. قوله: (هي القوَّة على فعل الشَّيء أو تركه): أي: الصَّلاحية للفعل والتّرك.
And the total statement on that: that bringing-into-existence, creating, providing, giving life, causing death, causing happiness, causing misery, and giving form, etc., according to the Ash'aris are temporal attributes because they are relations and considerations between power and the object of power. And according to the Maturidis they are eternal because they are an eternal attribute by which the world emanates, and every part of its parts, and it is called takwin. But if it is connected to the existence of a thing it is called bringing-into-existence and creating, or to its death it is called causing death, or to its form it is called giving form. And it is additional to power and will. So by will is specification, and power is the potency upon doing a thing or leaving it, and the relation of the two matters to it are equal. So by it (power) there is not the emanation of things; rather by it is the reception of emanation, so it is the principle of reception of emanation, and takwin is the principle of the emanation itself. According to him (the Maturidi) it is eternal and temporality is temporal. His saying: (but if it is connected, etc.): meaning it is named according to its object. His saying: (It is the potency upon doing a thing or leaving it): meaning the suitability for doing and leaving.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage provides a comparative summary of the Ash'ari and Maturidi positions on the attributes of acts. The author lists various attributes (bringing-into-existence, creating, providing, etc.) and states the Ash'ari view that they are temporal, being mere relations between power and its objects. The Maturidi view is that they are eternal, because they are aspects of a single eternal attribute called takwin. The text explains that the naming of these attributes (e.g., creating, causing death) depends on the specific object of relation. The author then clarifies the distinct roles of will (specification), power (ability to do or refrain), and takwin (actual emanation). Power only enables the reception of emanation; takwin is the direct principle of emanation. Finally, the author notes that according to the Maturidi, takwin is eternal while temporality is temporal. The commentary lines further explain that the attributes are named according to their objects, and that 'potency' means suitability for action or omission.

The Two Schools on Divine Acts: Temporary or Eternal?
Summary of Ash'ari and Maturidi positions on divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core difference between the Ash'ari and Maturidi positions on whether attributes like creating and providing are created or eternal.

Core Idea
Divine acts are either temporal relations or an eternal attribute called takwīn.

Al-Sawi opens this section by presenting the two major theological schools' stances on a key issue: are the divine acts (like creating, providing, giving life and death) themselves created attributes or eternal ones? This disagreement hinges on how each school understands the relationship between God's power and the objects of that power. Let’s read the passage and see how each school argues.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the parallel structure: 'inda al-Ash'ariyya... 'inda al-Māturīdiyya.
2
Identify the two schools
The passage explicitly names the Ash'ariyya and the Māturīdiyya. Mark each school's position.
3
Note what each school says about the nature of these attributes
Ash'aris say they are created (ḥāditha) and relational; Māturīdis say they are eternal (qadīma) and subsumed under takwīn.
4
Ask: why does the Ash'ari say they are 'additions and considerations'?
Reflect on the phrase 'iḍāfāt wa i'tibārāt bayna al-qudra wa al-maqdūr'. What does that imply about the reality of these attributes?
5
Contrast the eternal attribute 'takwīn' for Maturidis
Note that Maturidis posit a single eternal attribute, takwīn, from which all these acts emanate.
This is the key difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجملة القول في ذلك: أنَّ الإيجاد والخلق والرزق والإحياء والإماتة والإشقاء والإسعاد والتَّصوير إلى غير ذلك عند الأشعرية صفات حادثة؛ لأنَّها إضافات واعتبارات بين القدرة والمقدور . وعند الماتريدية قديمة؛ لأنَّها صفة أزليَّة بها صدور العالم، وكلّ جزء من أجزائه، ويسمى تكويناً، لكن إن تعلقت بوجود الشَّيء سميت إيجاداً وخلقاً، أو بموته سمّيت إماتة، أو بصورته سميت تصويراً، وهي زائدة على القدرة والإرادة، فالإرادة بها التَّخصيص، والقدرة هي القوَّة على فعل الشَّيء أو تركه، ونسبة الأمرين إليها على السواء، فليس بها صدور الأشياء، وإنَّما بها قبول الصُّدور، فهي مبدأ لقبول الصُّدور، والتكوين مبدأ لنفس الصُّدور . قوله : (لكن إن تعلقت ... إلخ)؛ أي: فتسمى باسم متعلقها . قوله : (هي القوَّة على فعل الشَّيء أو تركه) : أي : الصَّلاحية للفعل والتّرك . والمحققون من الأشاعرة على أنَّه ليس في الأزل إلا مبدأ الإيجاد والإشقاء والإسعاد وغير ذلك، ولا دليل على صفة أخرى سوى القدرة والإرادة، فإنَّ القدرة وإن كان نسبتها إلى وجود المكوّن وعدمه على السواء، لكن مع انضمام الإرادة يتخصص أحد الجانبين. وإِنَّما نصَّ على الإشقاء والإسعاد وإن دخلا في الإيجاد اهتماماً بشأنهما .
The summary statement in that: Indeed, ījād, khalq, rizq, iḥyā', imāta, ishqā', is'ād, taṣwīr, and so on, according to the Ash'ariyya, are created attributes, because they are additions and considerations between the power and the destined thing. According to the Māturīdiyya, they are eternal, because they are an eternal attribute through which emanates the world and every part of it, and it is called takwīn. But if it relates to the existence of a thing, it is called ījād and khalq; or to its death, it is called imāta; or to its form, it is called taṣwīr. And it is superadded to qudra and irāda. Thus irāda specifies, and qudra is the power to do or leave a thing, and the ratio of the two is equal to it; so not by it is the emanation of things, but rather by it is the acceptance of emanation; so it is the principle of acceptance of emanation, and takwīn is the principle of emanation itself. He said: (But if it relates... etc.) i.e., it is named after its object. He said: (It is the power to do or leave a thing) i.e., the capability for action and non-action. And the verificators among the Ash'ariyya hold that there is in pre-eternity only the principle of ījād, ishqā', is'ād, and so on, and there is no evidence for another attribute besides qudra and irāda. Indeed, qudra, although its relation to the existence and non-existence of the created thing is equal, yet with the addition of irāda, one side becomes specified. And he specifically mentioned ishqā' and is'ād, although they are included in ījād, out of concern for their significance.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a comparative summary of the Ash'ari and Maturidi positions on the attributes of divine acts. It begins by listing several divine acts (ījād, khalq, rizq, iḥyā', imāta, ishqā', is'ād, taṣwīr) and states the Ash'ari view: these are created (ḥāditha) attributes, because they are relational considerations between qudra (power) and the object (maqdūr). The Maturidi view follows: these are eternal (qadīma), all belonging to a single eternal attribute called takwīn (origination), which is the principle through which the world and every part of it emanate. However, when this attribute relates to a specific object, it takes the name of that relation (e.g., ījād for bringing into existence). The passage then explains that takwīn is superadded (zā'ida) to qudra and irāda (will). Irāda is the specifying principle, qudra is the power to act or refrain (with equal relation), so qudra alone does not cause emanation; it is merely the principle of acceptance of emanation. Takwīn, in contrast, is the principle of emanation itself. The commentary interlinearly clarifies that the attribute is named after its object and that 'power' here means capability (ṣalāḥiyya). Finally, the muḥaqqiqūn (verificators) among the Ash'ariyya are cited: they hold that in pre-eternity (azal) there is only the principle of these acts, not separate attributes, and that specifying emerges from the combination of qudra and irāda. The specific mention of ishqā' and is'ād is intentional, to emphasize their significance despite being included under ījād.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that both schools agree these attributes are separate eternal entities.
Correction: Ash'aris consider them temporal relations; Maturidis consider them aspects of a single eternal attribute.

Checkpoint

A) Because they are physical actions that happen in time.

C) Because they are independent attributes of God.
D) Because they occur after non-existence.

Key Takeaway
Ash'aris view divine acts as temporal relations, while Maturidis view them as manifestations of an eternal attribute takwīn.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Qudra, Irāda, and Takwīn: Their Roles and Relationships
Elaboration on the Maturidi concept of takwīn and its relationship with qudra and irāda.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctions between qudra (power), irāda (will), and takwīn (origination) as presented in the Maturidi view.

Core Idea
Qudra enables acceptance of emanation; Takwīn causes it.

Further elaborating on the Maturidi position, Al-Sawi explains how the attribute of takwīn relates to qudra and irāda. He clarifies that qudra alone is not sufficient for emanation; it is only the principle of acceptance, while takwīn is the principle of emanation itself. This lesson unpacks those definitions and the naming of the attribute after its object.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on naming based on object
Notice how the same takwīn attribute takes different names depending on whether it relates to existence, death, or form.
2
Identify the definitions of irāda and qudra
Irāda is the specifying principle; qudra is the power to do or leave, with equal relation to both.
3
Understand the difference between qudra's role and takwīn's role
Qudra is the principle of acceptance of emanation; takwīn is the principle of emanation itself.
This is the key distinction.
4
Reflect on why qudra's relation to existence and non-existence is equal
Because qudra alone does not necessitate one side; it is a neutral capacity.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجملة القول في ذلك: أنَّ الإيجاد والخلق والرزق والإحياء والإماتة والإشقاء والإسعاد والتَّصوير إلى غير ذلك عند الأشعرية صفات حادثة؛ لأنَّها إضافات واعتبارات بين القدرة والمقدور . وعند الماتريدية قديمة؛ لأنَّها صفة أزليَّة بها صدور العالم، وكلّ جزء من أجزائه، ويسمى تكويناً، لكن إن تعلقت بوجود الشَّيء سميت إيجاداً وخلقاً، أو بموته سمّيت إماتة، أو بصورته سميت تصويراً، وهي زائدة على القدرة والإرادة، فالإرادة بها التَّخصيص، والقدرة هي القوَّة على فعل الشَّيء أو تركه، ونسبة الأمرين إليها على السواء، فليس بها صدور الأشياء، وإنَّما بها قبول الصُّدور، فهي مبدأ لقبول الصُّدور، والتكوين مبدأ لنفس الصُّدور . قوله : (لكن إن تعلقت ... إلخ)؛ أي: فتسمى باسم متعلقها . قوله : (هي القوَّة على فعل الشَّيء أو تركه) : أي : الصَّلاحية للفعل والتّرك . والمحققون من الأشاعرة على أنَّه ليس في الأزل إلا مبدأ الإيجاد والإشقاء والإسعاد وغير ذلك، ولا دليل على صفة أخرى سوى القدرة والإرادة، فإنَّ القدرة وإن كان نسبتها إلى وجود المكوّن وعدمه على السواء، لكن مع انضمام الإرادة يتخصص أحد الجانبين. وإِنَّما نصَّ على الإشقاء والإسعاد وإن دخلا في الإيجاد اهتماماً بشأنهما .
The summary statement in that: Indeed, ījād, khalq, rizq, iḥyā', imāta, ishqā', is'ād, taṣwīr, and so on, according to the Ash'ariyya, are created attributes, because they are additions and considerations between the power and the destined thing. According to the Māturīdiyya, they are eternal, because they are an eternal attribute through which emanates the world and every part of it, and it is called takwīn. But if it relates to the existence of a thing, it is called ījād and khalq; or to its death, it is called imāta; or to its form, it is called taṣwīr. And it is superadded to qudra and irāda. Thus irāda specifies, and qudra is the power to do or leave a thing, and the ratio of the two is equal to it; so not by it is the emanation of things, but rather by it is the acceptance of emanation; so it is the principle of acceptance of emanation, and takwīn is the principle of emanation itself. He said: (But if it relates... etc.) i.e., it is named after its object. He said: (It is the power to do or leave a thing) i.e., the capability for action and non-action. And the verificators among the Ash'ariyya hold that there is in pre-eternity only the principle of ījād, ishqā', is'ād, and so on, and there is no evidence for another attribute besides qudra and irāda. Indeed, qudra, although its relation to the existence and non-existence of the created thing is equal, yet with the addition of irāda, one side becomes specified. And he specifically mentioned ishqā' and is'ād, although they are included in ījād, out of concern for their significance.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a comparative summary of the Ash'ari and Maturidi positions on the attributes of divine acts. It begins by listing several divine acts (ījād, khalq, rizq, iḥyā', imāta, ishqā', is'ād, taṣwīr) and states the Ash'ari view: these are created (ḥāditha) attributes, because they are relational considerations between qudra (power) and the object (maqdūr). The Maturidi view follows: these are eternal (qadīma), all belonging to a single eternal attribute called takwīn (origination), which is the principle through which the world and every part of it emanate. However, when this attribute relates to a specific object, it takes the name of that relation (e.g., ījād for bringing into existence). The passage then explains that takwīn is superadded (zā'ida) to qudra and irāda (will). Irāda is the specifying principle, qudra is the power to act or refrain (with equal relation), so qudra alone does not cause emanation; it is merely the principle of acceptance of emanation. Takwīn, in contrast, is the principle of emanation itself. The commentary interlinearly clarifies that the attribute is named after its object and that 'power' here means capability (ṣalāḥiyya). Finally, the muḥaqqiqūn (verificators) among the Ash'ariyya are cited: they hold that in pre-eternity (azal) there is only the principle of these acts, not separate attributes, and that specifying emerges from the combination of qudra and irāda. The specific mention of ishqā' and is'ād is intentional, to emphasize their significance despite being included under ījād.

Key Terms
التكوين
القدرة
الإرادة
التخصيص
الصدور
القبول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that qudra alone is sufficient to bring things into existence.
Correction: Qudra is only the principle of acceptance; takwīn is the principle of emanation.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say is the role of qudra in relation to emanation?
A) It directly causes emanation.
B) It is the principle of acceptance of emanation.
C) It specifies which thing comes into existence.
D) It is identical to takwīn.

Key Takeaway
Qudra is the capacity to receive emanation; takwīn is the active principle that brings it about.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan your day, do you truly believe that your will (irāda) only specifies what you intend, and your power (qudra) is merely a capacity to accept Allah's takwīn? How does this reshape your reliance on Him for every action?
?
If takwīn is the attribute that actively brings things into existence, and it takes different names (ījād, imāta, taṣwīr) based on the object, then every event—your waking, your breath, your thoughts—is a direct act of that attribute. Have you been living as if outcomes depend on your own power? What would it mean for you to see Allah's takwīn in every moment?
?
The passage says qudra is equally related to doing and leaving, meaning it does not determine which occurs. Irāda specifies, and takwīn enacts. Does this challenge your sense of control? Will you consciously acknowledge today that even your choices are only possible because Allah's takwīn brings them into being?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
The Ash'ari Verificators' Position on Divine Acts
Ash'ari verificators' position on divine attributes in pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refined Ash'ari position that only qudra and irāda are necessary attributes in pre-eternity, and how irāda specifies the equal capacity of qudra.

Core Idea
In pre-eternity, only qudra and irāda exist; divine acts are their relational consequences.

After presenting the standard Ash'ari and Maturidi views, Al-Sawi introduces the position of the muḥaqqiqūn (verificators) among the Ash'aris. They refine the earlier Ash'ari view by asserting that in pre-eternity (azal) there is no separate attribute for each divine act; rather, only qudra and irāda suffice. This lesson examines their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage detailing the Ash'ari verificators' claim
Pay attention to what they say exists in pre-eternity and what they reject.
2
Understand how qudra with irāda leads to specification
Qudra is equally related to existence and non-existence; irāda tips the balance.
3
Note why they mention ishqā' and is'ād specifically
Although these are included in ījād, they are singled out for emphasis due to their importance.
4
Compare with the earlier Ash'ari view
This verified view is more minimal: no need for multiple created attributes, just qudra and irāda.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception: Thinking that the Ash'ari verificators reject the need for irāda, or that they believe qudra alone suffices.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari verificators, what is the role of irāda in relation to qudra?
A) Irāda increases qudra's power.
B) Irāda specifies which side qudra acts upon.
C) Irāda creates the objects directly.
D) Irāda is unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari verificators affirm that qudra and irāda are sufficient; irāda specifies qudra's equal relation to existence and non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a setback or hardship (ishqā'), do you immediately recognize it as coming from Allah's qudra and irāda, or do you instinctively blame others or yourself? How can you train your heart to see His hand in every situation?
?
The lesson teaches that qudra alone is neutral; it is irāda that specifies. In your life, do you acknowledge that your own will is subject to Allah's irāda? What does this imply about your plans and ambitions? Will you surrender them to Him today?
?
If Allah's acts of making wretched (ishqā') and making happy (is'ād) are both from His will, how does this shape your attitude toward those who are suffering? Do you see them as tests or punishments? How can this lesson increase your reliance on His mercy and justice?

Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
Ash'ari Position on Divine Attributes in Pre-Eternity
Al-Sawi states the Ash'ari position on divine attributes in pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that in pre-eternity only power and will are proven attributes, and that all divine actions (creating, causing misery, causing happiness) are expressions of these.

Core Idea
In pre-eternity, only power and will are affirmed; actions like creation are their effects.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary clarifies a key Ash'ari doctrine: in pre-eternity, the only proven attributes of Allah are power and will. All divine acts, including creation and the determination of happiness or misery, are not separate attributes but outcomes of will specifying power. The passage also explains why the text highlights misery and happiness despite their being part of creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get the overall meaning. Note the precise wording used by Al-Sawi.
2
Identify the key claims
Notice that the passage states that in pre-eternity, only the principles of creation, misery, and happiness exist, and that there is no evidence for any attribute besides power and will. Understand the role of will in specifying the effect of power.
3
Understand the emphasis on misery and happiness
Reflect on why the author specifically mentions causing misery and causing happiness. The passage says it is out of concern for their importance, even though they are included in 'bringing into existence'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمحققون من الأشاعرة على أنَّه ليس في الأزل إلا مبدأ الإيجاد والإشقاء والإسعاد وغير ذلك، ولا دليل على صفة أخرى سوى القدرة والإرادة، فإنَّ القدرة وإن كان نسبتها إلى وجود المكوّن وعدمه على السواء، لكن مع انضمام الإرادة يتخصص أحد الجانبين. وإِنَّما نصَّ على الإشقاء والإسعاد وإن دخلا في الإيجاد اهتماماً بشأنهما .
The verified scholars among the Ash'aris hold that in pre-eternity there is only the principle of bringing into existence, causing misery, causing happiness, and other than that, and there is no evidence for another attribute besides power and will. For power, even though its relation to the existence and non-existence of the contingent is equal, yet with the joining of will, one of the two sides becomes specified. And he only specified [the text] with causing misery and causing happiness, even though they are included in bringing into existence, out of concern for their importance.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage states the Ash'ari position on the divine attributes in pre-eternity. The author explains that the verified Ash'aris hold that only the action of bringing into existence (al-ījād) is present, along with its specific manifestations of misery (ishqā') and happiness (is'ād). These are not separate attributes but are the result of will. The passage emphasizes that there is no evidence for any attribute other than power and will. The power of God is equal with respect to creating or not creating something, but when will is added, one particular possibility becomes determined. The final sentence explains that the text specified these two effects (misery and happiness) to highlight their significance, even though they are subsumed under creation.

الإيجاد
الإشقاء
الإسعاد

الإرادة
المكوّن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'aris deny that Allah has any attributes at all.
Correction: The passage shows that Ash'aris affirm power and will as proven attributes, while considering other descriptions like creation as effects, not separate attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the verified Ash'aris hold about pre-eternity?
A) Only power and will exist as attributes.
B) Only the principle of creation, misery, and happiness exist.
C) All divine attributes are eternal.
D) Only power exists.

Key Takeaway
The verified Ash'ari position is that only power and will are proven attributes in pre-eternity; all other divine actions are effects of these.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If only God's power and will determine whether you experience misery or happiness, how does that affect the way you respond to personal trials? Will you commit to seeing every event as a specific choice of His will, and adjust your expectations accordingly?
?
The passage emphasizes that will is what specifies outcomes. In what area of your life are you acting as if your own planning is sufficient, ignoring that without God's will nothing happens? What concrete step can you take today to acknowledge His will in that matter?
?
Causing misery and happiness are highlighted as important effects. Think of one person you know who is in misery or happiness right now. How can your belief that these are directly from God's power and will change your prayer for them and your own emotional response?
